And I remember driving through Woomera and thinking I should stop there to check out the rocket range museum. But I didn’t do that either. I just kept on driving.

Upon arriving in Adelaide, after having Dan stolen from me by that Adelaidian Junior clown cop, and after walking all the way back to that motel I’d just checked in to in Glen Osmand, I remember reading about that car accident Anthony Albenese (the future prime minister of Australia) was involved in. It sounded pretty serious. (Victorian drivers probably.) I hoped he was okay. I also remember wondering if all his airbags deployed.

I can’t prove it, but I’m firmly convinced the South Australian Liberal Party Police State government deliberately targeted me for ruin because of that Adelaide, City of Sex Robots piece I’d written a few months earlier, after my first visit to Adelaide. Such a pity. I was planning on driving over to Perth and then up to Broome next. But sadly, Darwin to Adelaide must stand as Dan’s final run.

Thus, Dan’s outback adventure has now ended, thanks to the all-pervasive power-abusing all-white middle-aged South Australian Liberal Party Police State government. I hereby declare the Australian “Liberal” Party an existential threat to Australian democracy. It should also be declared an illegally funded far-right domestic terrorist organisation. Not that I can go anywhere else anyway. Ran out of money. And now my Australian Capital Territory driver’s license just expired. Now I’m really going to start fucking with them.

I wonder if I could apply for a grant from the South Australian Liberal Party Police State government so we can start development on that medicinal marijuana delivery device and app we’ve always wanted to build. Then we could control the method of induction, how its grown, the strain, quantity and the quality (Sativa/Indica, THC/CBD levels, etc.), instead of being forever at the mercy of whatever shitty bush weed or pepped-up hydro crap is available, spiked with whatever and who knows what. We’d get more work done. Of course, it would have to be invite only, and only local Adelaide delivery to start. And we’d probably also have to sell something legal in the same packaging so drivers don’t know what they’re delivering. Coffee, perhaps? Or maybe we could use delivery drones? We need to mission drive this one. Remove the keystone predator species and the entire narcotics ecosystem collapses. Don’t wait for the law to change, just go out and do it. They can’t arrest all of us.

That’s all probably just another one of my crazy pipe dreams, just like defecting to China. I seriously don’t know what to do or where to go. How do I escape this wretched state of societally enforced solitude and state-propelled perpetual penury? But it looks as if every state in Australia is permanently sealing off it borders now anyway – apparently to prevent the spread of West Australian separatists and people fleeing the Melbourne lockdowns – so I can’t really go anywhere else. And even if I could, Dan is no longer with me.

I miss Dan so much. I only feel at home when I’m moving. And not only that, now I have no one to talk to. I wonder where she is? Did they tow her off to the wrecking yard? Or is she being put to other uses? Maybe Dan can still hear me, wherever she is?

Dan! What am I going to do?

Go back to Melbourne, whispers Dan.

No thanks.

Canberra then.

Fuck that.

Well, you should have listened to me before when I told you to go across the top to Broome. Now you’re stuck here in Adelaide, aren’t you? And stop talking to me. I’m not here anymore.

True enough.

I’ll never drive around Australia again, and never again during a deadly global pandemic. My fate seems to depend on which state government is in power. I really should have listened to Dan and gone across the top to Broome and then down to Perth. Maybe I should sell Betty and buy a plane ticket to Perth? I could join up with all the other residentially challenged over there. Or maybe I should go back to Queensland? I really don’t know what to do. I love Queensland, but I’ve never been to Western Australia. I’m clearly in a state of overstated state power flummox. I’ve visited if not lived in every state and territory in Australia now, except Western Australia, and I must say, without exception, Queensland surpasses them all – except Western Australia. May Queensland secede and take all the rest of us with her! – except Western Australia.

Abolish the states!

Please excuse the outburst. I believe I’m still suffering from separation anxiety, and the associated depression. Yet more, I know. What else can they take away from me, I wonder? How else can they go out of their way to make my life even more miserable? I think they’re trying to get me to commit partial suicide again. But I don’t think I’ll need to this time. I’ll probably just end up dying here soon anyway in a state of non-productive squalor from excruciating boredom and deep depression. At least it’s quiet here, so I can get some real work done – albeit unpaid work. And most of the people here, the non-govcrims, are fine upstanding citizens (unless they’re from Glen Osmond). Nonetheless, it’s become more than obvious to me now that I can never work in this country again. They’ll just target me endlessly for being a crazy old Aboriginal woman who does her own LED lighting upgrades. I think they’re about to cut my unemployment benefits too, so now I’m really fucked. I might need to sell my guitar for food and rent soon. Then I suppose it’s back to prostitution again – an inevitable return to the good old oral tradition. But I’m far too old for that kind of thing now, and I don’t think I could ever really defect to China. With my mouth, I’d be in prison within a week and dead within a month. So I’ll probably just have to revert back to being a 23-year-old semi-suicidal hikikomori.

Someone bring me a tantō and a can of kerosene!

Ode to Adelaide, City of Sex Robots

My sexbot foeti are now nurtured within the womb of the City of Sex Robots,
Gently bathed in warm synthetic amniotic fluid,
Freely flowing fluidly all over and around — as warm free-flowing fluid generally does.
Adelaide!

In the European carp of the Karrawirraparri, in the marauding feral cats of the Mount Lofty Ranges,
In the long-since evaporated clouds of the longest of dry hot summer days,
In the fallow fields of the withered vineyards, thy sex robotic conception potentials beam forth,
Adelaide!

Gale-force winds tear through the clattering eucalyptus leaves,
As hordes of common commuters bustle back uniformly to their sprawling suburbs of endless oblivion,
The waves of Henley beach roar and Rainbow Lorikeets fall from the sky — yet fear not,
Adelaide!

Some day, o miracle! we shall deliver sex robots together of truly awesome power,
Upon my pauper’s grave, and from the ashes of my forced early retirement;
And clearly on every sexbot compliance plate shall there be engraved:
Adelaide!

Open Letter to Dolly Parton

Hi, Dolly.

Just to let you know, I haven’t been vaccinated yet. But I live in Australia, so don’t hold your breath. Not that it matters much, since I’m forever socially distanced and permanently self-isolated. But I will get vaccinated soon, I promise – if I can ever leave the house again.

I hope you don’t mind that I’m writing to you. I’m only doing so because you are the reigning Queen of Country, and because I believe myself to be the reincarnation of Jimmie Rodgers. I think rather highly of myself, don’t I? What are you saying? Jimmie Rodgers is an absolute god! I know. But that’s nothing. I used to think I was the reincarnation of Christ. But that was back when I wasn’t smoking enough marijuana. Now I am smoking enough marijuana, but I’m still very unhappy.

You see, I’m in love with a woman who lives in a country I can’t get to right now. I’ve never met her before, or even spoken to her, and I’m sure she has absolutely no interest in me. Yet I sincerely believe my unspoken love for her to be quite real. I must be insane, right? But I’m sure you must be familiar with this phenomenon. Surely you’ve experienced much the same thing yourself – sad, lonely old men idolising you from afar. I’m pathetic, I know.

Like you, she is a talented and successful artist. Also like you, she is a beautiful woman with many admirers (and suitors, I imagine). Her name is not Jolene, and her eyes are not of emerald green, yet her beauty is beyond compare, and she does have flaming locks of auburn hair (or at least she did at one time) and a voice like summer rain. What intrigues me about her most, however, is her voice, I swear.

I’m not stalking her, I’m really not. I did take a look at one of her social media profiles a few days ago, but I only spent a few seconds on the page, I swear. Yet time enough to notice a hairy muscular human arm in one of the pictures of her dog. I assume it’s her dog, not her arm. Whose arm is it then? Her partner, in all likelihood. I hope not, but I assume so.

Nonetheless, even if that hairy arm does belong to a pre-existing paramour, I really don’t care. I must sing and play Everything’s Beautiful (In Its Own Way) with her, in Japanese, and then propose marriage in a Japanese tea garden. I know that sounds completely crazy, but I simply must. I have no time left. It may take me several years to do so – especially if Mister Hairy Arms is indeed her present partner – yet eventually I know I shall succeed. She’s the one. This time I’m sure.

I know I’ve said that before, but this time I really am sure.

How can I be so absolutely sure about a woman I’ve never met before? Well, for one thing she likes dogs. She also plays the fiddle and knows a lot about kabuki. What else do I need to know?

Okay, I’m sure there’s much more I need to know. Regardless, I believe I’m now sufficiently equipped with enough intelligence to begin my suit.

Of course, I’ve been wrong before. I’ve made some very bad decisions in the past, the repercussive trauma of which I’m still recovering from. And I suppose that’s one of the reasons why I’m writing to you today.

As My Queen, Dolly, I must humbly beseech your blessing in commencing this courtship. Since I’ve made so many stupid mistakes of this nature before, and since I’m still paying the cost, my confidence in my own faculties of personal discernment has since been compromised quite considerably. Your blessing would mean so much to me.

The other reason I’m writing to you today is to ask you for a loan. I only have $5 left and have to pay rent tomorrow. I could pawn my guitar again, I suppose. But I’ve been doing that since I was 23. I really don’t see why I should be forced to continue doing so. $23,000 should be enough. I can pay it back in full within 12 months – and with 11% interest. I’m sorry to have to ask you to do this, but I really have no one else to turn to.

I know that’s quite a lot to ask, considering you’ve never met me before and have no idea who I am. Yet I assure you I am precisely that which I believe myself to be, and I will accomplish all I set out to accomplish. But I refuse to pawn my guitar again, I simply refuse. I must have her!

And I will get vaccinated as soon as I can, I promise.

Thanks, Dolly.

Love always.

Update: As of October 26, 2021, I am at last doubly vaccinated (AstraZeneca).

Update Two: And as of January 18, 2023 I am quadrupally vaccinated (AstraZeneca, Moderna, Pfizer, etc.). I’m addicted to these things now. I can’t get enough of them.

Young Kosaburo Eto, Who Set Himself on Fire

Kosaburo Eto was 23 when he set himself on fire. He did so for reasons I can never even begin to understand. I’m sorry, but that’s just the way I am. I can understand setting oneself on fire for a woman, but never for a political cause. Of course, that woman would have to be truly worthy of setting oneself on fire.

Not that I’m about to set myself on fire. But if I were about to set myself on fire, I would write the following jisei and send it to you:

Young Kosaburo Eto, who set himself on fire,
Once loved a woman, who did not set herself on fire.
Kosaburo loved her more than he despised his enemies.
In truth, he set himself on fire for her.
It was for want of her love that Kosaburo died.

I know that’s not the true reason Kosaburo set himself on fire. But I just fail to understand how young Kosaburo could commit suicide at such an early age for any other reason, other than for love. How else could one dare to act with a true Yamato spirit?

Niggers Don’t Know How to Poo

I do apologise for using the word nigger again. I was going to title this piece, The Highly Unsanitary Singaporean-Adelaidean-Managed Croydon Park Cockroach-Infested Boarding House from Over-Signed HELL. But that’s a bit too long, isn’t it?

Seriously, I’ve never seen so many cockroaches in all my life. They’ve taken over the entire kitchen. So I’m withholding rent (I don’t have the money anyway) until my Singaporean-Adelaidean landlord gets rid of all the cockroaches – and removes all the racist how-to-poo signs in the toilet. Yes, there are also racist how-to-poo signs in the toilet. Because niggers don’t know how to poo, they need three signs to show them what to do.

First Sign: Sit on the toilet seat, don’t stand on it.

Second Sign: Poo into the toilet bowl, not on the floor.

Third Sign: Clean up when you are done, and don’t forget to flush. And do not leave poo on the floor. Yesterday I found poo on the floor and had to clean it up. Yuck!!! It was disgusting! I will charge $200 for extra poo floor cleaning if I see poo on the floor again.

Nigger to Third Sign: Which day was yesterday?

Adelaide, Australia, 2021

An Interfering Journalist in the Korean War

13 June, 2005

Executions for political reasons began when Seoul was recaptured by the allies [as if they never occurred when Seoul was first captured by the North!], and when the South became threatened again they increased at an alarming rate.

John Colless, an Australian working for AAP-Reuter, reported that the police shot fifty-six political prisoners alongside the Sariwon railway station and then watched American troops give first aid to those who had not died outright....

One correspondent took direct personal action to stop the executions. He was Alan Dower, of the Melbourne Herald. Dower, a former commando officer, was driving into Seoul with [the BBC’s Rene] Cutforth and a cameraman, Cyril Page, when they passed a column of women, many carrying babies, and wearing straw masks over their heads, being escorted by South Korean policemen. Dower stopped the jeep and asked what was happening. “These Communists,” a policeman said. “They go be shot, executed.” Dower said, “What? Babies Communist? Who say they Communist?” The policeman looked puzzled. “People say. People in street point and say that person Communist.” The three correspondents followed the column to a gaol on a hill at the outskirts of Seoul and watched the heavy gates clang behind it. Then Dower, who was armed, thudded on a peep-hole with the butt of his carbine. When a policeman’s face appeared, Dower pointed the gun at him and threatened to shoot him if he did not open the gates. Inside, the correspondents saw the column of women and children kneeling alongside a deep, freshly dug pit. On the other side were two machine guns. “Hell,” Dower said, “this is a bloody fine set-up to lose good Australian lives over. I’m going to do something about this.” The correspondents stormed into the office of the gaol’s governor and found him sitting behind his desk. Dower aimed his carbine and said, “If those machine guns fire I’ll shoot you between the eyes.” After the governor promised that the guns would not fire and that there would be no executions, Dower threatened that if he failed to keep his word Dower would seek him out and kill him.

In Seoul, Dower went to United Nations officials and told them what had happened. “They pleaded with me not to make an international incident out of it. I told them that I had sent my paper an outline of the story, but if there were any more executions, then I’d send a story that would rock the world. They promised to see that there would be no more women and children death marches and as far as I could find out there weren’t.” But what had already been published, by Dower and by a few other correspondents, mostly non-American, caused a wave of disillusionment with the South Korean regime and with the war in general. The British Sunday newspaper Reynolds News summed up this feeling: “Terrible things are being done in Korea in your name. They are being done by Syngman Rhee’s police sheltering behind US and British United Nations troops.”

SOURCE: The First Casualty: The War Correspondent as Hero and Myth-Maker from the Crimea to Kosovo, by Phillip Knightley, with an introduction by John Pilger (Johns Hopkins U. Press, 2000; first published in 1975), pp. 374-376.

Women Sang for this Strangler

By ALAN DOWER, The Herald Police Reporter

There is nothing more chilling in the files of the Victorian Police Department than the confessions of Edward Joseph Leonski, the young American soldier who made women laugh and sing before he throttled them.

Even the fear of “Jack the S t r a n g l e r” that swept through London recently was not greater than the “black out murders” terror that gripped Melbourne almost 11 years ago.

Leonski struck at scattered points. He murdered three times and savagely attacked other women before police had one clue to his identity.

He prowled through blacked-out streets when the Japanese invasion scare was at its peak, when nerves were frayed and the crime-fighting strength of the police force was weakened by services enlistments and A.R.P. control.

Leonski caused the biggest manhunt in the history of the Victorian CIB. His name, even after he was hanged, was an embarrassment to the U.S. forces in Australia.

His name will never be forgotten by the 50 detectives who hunted him night and day. It will never be forgotten by students of crime history who have tried to understand his psychopathic mind.

★

Eleven years ago this month, Melbourne people’s eyes goggled when they saw an American soldier – later identified as Leonski – drinking in the city bars.

He seemed to be “just a good guy.” A strange one, though! He mixed beer, whisky, ice cream, mustard, ketchup and hot peppers and drained his glass with apparent relish.

Women giggled when they saw him walking on his hands for several minutes. Most did not hear – and those who did shrugged it off at first – his whispered talk of werewolf howls, of split personalities, of Jekyll and Hyde.

Only a few noticed the occasional glazed look in his eyes, the clenching of his strong hands, his random talk of “soft women,” “nice voices,” and how he cried the day he left Texas for duty overseas.

Just a strange American, they said. “A good-time Yank down under.”

It was only a few weeks before the U.S. court martial which condemned him to death described him as “Baby face – but vicious underneath” . . .

On May 3, 1942, the body of Mrs Ivy Violet McLeod was found In a door recess at Albert Park. She had been strangled, and most of her clothes were torn off.

There were no clues. Someone had heard a man running, but no one had seen the strangler.

Six nights later – May 9 – Mrs Pauline Buchan Thomson, a policeman’s wife, was strangled at the gate of an apartment house in Spring Street, City. Her clothes had been ripped from her body.

There was a slender clue. From 9.15 p.m. until midnight, Mrs Thomson had been seen drinking with an American serviceman at a city hotel. But there were thousands of Americans in Melbourne.

Within three days, police history was made at Russell Street. Detectives dressed a window dummy with the dead woman’s clothes and superimposed a photograph of her face on the dummy’s head.

It was a life-like reconstruction. Photographs were published in all newspapers, but they did not yield a clue.

The chiefs at Russell Street were becoming restless. Many reports – most of them reliable – had been received from women who had been attacked and almost strangled at night.

Police listed the names of 1000 suspects in Australia and shadowed every known criminal day and night.

On the night of May 18, attractive Miss Gladys Hosking was murdered near a muddy ARP slit trench at Royal Park.

Next day Melbourne women were warned not to walk through blacked-out streets without an escort.

The police were now certain of only three things. Their suspect was an American soldier. He had very strong hands and probably was well-built. He was probably stationed at Camp Pell.

Certain that unless they worked fast another girl would die, the police in the next four days knocked on every door down three miles of streets near Royal Park, and questioned 500 people.

They drew a blank – until suddenly they met an Australian soldier who was in Royal Park the night the girl was murdered.

Yes, he remembered having seen a well-knit young American soldier groping through the dark toward Camp Pell. He was plastered with yellow mud. The American had mumbled something about finding Area One.

Area One! Yellow mud! There was only one large patch of mustard-colored mud near Camp Pell – around the silt trench where the body had been found.

On May 22, the Australian soldier identified Leonski in an identification parade of well-knit young Americans.

★

IN the presence of police and his own army officers, Leonski signed three confessions.

He admitted he killed Mrs McLeod. “She smiled at me from a doorway,” he said. “Then I had my arms around her.... I changed the position of my hands and grabbed her at the front of the throat. I squeezed...and she fell rapidly....”

He paused, then said: “I remember about the girl who was killed in Spring Street. I met her in a restaurant. She was singing in my ear.... We left the restaurant (hotel) and turned the corner. There was nobody around. I just heard her voice. I grabbed her around the neck. She stopped singing.... I said ‘Keep singing.’ She fell down. I got mad then and tore at her.... She would not sing.... How could she sing?...”

Leonski signed this confession and then told police how he met Gladys Hosking in the Parkville Hotel.

“She was a small girl,” he said. “She was carrying an umbrella. I asked if I could walk with her and she said ‘AH right.’ We walked until we came to her house. She had a lovely voice.

“I wanted that voice.... She was leaving me.... I grabbed her by the throat. I choked her.... She didn’t even make a sound.”

— The Herald (Melbourne, Vic. : 1861 - 1954), April 11, 1953. Page 14.

  1. All public board, tribunal, and statutory appointments should be advertised, along with the selection criteria for each position.
  2. An independent panel, including the relevant departmental secretary and a new Public Appointments Commissioner, or their representatives, should assess applications against the selection criteria and provide a shortlist of suitable candidates to the minister.
  3. The minister should choose from the shortlist, or redefine and republish the selection criteria, but should not directly select any candidate not shortlisted.
  4. Reappointments should be made by an independent panel, but need not be re-advertised.
  5. Federal and state governments should legislate this new process for public appointments.
  6. A new Public Appointments Commissioner should report to parliament on board and tribunal appointments and publish an annual report.
  7. The Public Service Commissioner should report to parliament on statutory appointments to the public service.

— New Politics: A better process for public appointments (July 2022), Page 4.

Canberra is made up of seven distinct districts containing a combined total of 123 suburbs (all of which look exactly the same) arranged in the shape of the letter Y, with a quasi-esoteric Trinitarian Masonic symbol known as the Parliamentary Triangle at its centre. Canberra is governed by a legislative assembly made up of 25 scared old white geezers with nothing better to do with their time (the descendants of land-thieving British pastoralists), assisted by the Australian Federal Police. People in Canberra are generally more educated and commit fewer crimes than in most other parts of Australia (unless they pretend to work at “Abo” institutes). Consequently, wages and rents are also higher and unemployment usually lower. Overall, it’s not such a bad place to live. That’s why Canberra is often voted the third most boring city to live in the world, after Geneva and Singapore. And I suppose that’s also why a lot of people from so-called Great Britain choose to live there. 33% of the population are born overseas, most of whom are British; and only 1.4% of the population identify as Aboriginal, all of them predominantly British; which means 65.6% of the entire population is mostly British. The other 34.4% stay home all day growing and smoking a lot of marijuana. Canberra is also known as “The Bush Weed Capital of Australia”. It took over from Adelaide during Covid. In fact, Canberra is the only place in Australia where most drugs are legal. But that’s only because most people who live there work for the government. A constant reminder of this fact is Mount Hypodermic, otherwise known as Telstra Tower, a digital data surveillance collection point shaped like a syringe that towers above the landscape and is visible from just about every part of the city. About the only other point of interest in Canberra is the Australian National Gallery. They have a Rothko and a Soulages and quite an extensive collection of Australian indigenous art. I used to go there sometimes to pay my respects. They also have a Jackson Pollock, a truly hideous squiggly mess of a thing. The Pollock is guarded at all times by proximity-preventing red laser beams and a real-life human security guard. The Rothko and the Soulages are not guarded at any time, nor is any of the Australian indigenous art.

They did so so they could misappropriate, miscategorise and glass case Australian indigenous cultures before they all went extinct – effectively, a white-washed academic “tag and bag” operation.

The “Abo” Institute’s Founding Principal (or CEO and founder, in the common parlance of our time) was a semi-professional Scottish-Canadian cyclist and backyard “movie” producer named Jim. Jim was also president of the Australian National University Cycling Club. Jim established a long tradition of ethno-filmological research at the “Abo” Institute, which still continues to this day: biking his way out into the remote desert regions of Australia to make unique and irreplaceable, spiritually significant “movies” about poor little “Abo” boys while they roll around naked in the dirt; filming them without their consent as they dance about wildly in culturally sensitive ways for whitey, etc. Sadly, not much seems to have changed to this day. And in 1974 a mob of real Aboriginal people wrote an open letter to the “Abo” Institute complaining about most of the staff there being white and all the money being spent on backwards-facing buildings and making “movies”. This letter became known as the “Eaglehawk and Crow letter”. But good luck finding a copy of it today, so here’s a Ngiyaampaa dreamtime story about Eaglehawk and Crow instead:


Eaglehawk and Crow

Long, long time ago Eaglehawk, it was his turn to go hunting. So Eaglehawk had a little baby, and he asked Crow, he went over to his neighbour Crow and asked Crow if he’d look after his baby while he went hunting, because food was getting much scarcer now and they had to go much further and further away from the camp.

So Eaglehawk, he went to Crow and asked him. Crow didn’t want to look after the baby, he said “No, no I don’t want to look after the baby, he’s crying too much, he’ll cry all the time and disturb the camp”. But Eaglehawk said, “No, he’ll be right, Crow”. He said, “You take him away and you sit down there and talk to him, or sing to him and he’ll quieten down”. Crow was still reluctant to take the baby, he said, “No, I don’t want to look after the kid”.

So anyway, Eaglehawk just handed the baby to Crow and said, “Okay, when we come back, whatever meat we get we’ll bring it back and we’ll share it with you”. Crow had to be satisfied with that and Eaglehawk just went off with his young men and of course they had to go a long, long way from the camp.

But Crow, after he got the baby, he took it into his gunyah, his hut, and he sat down there with the baby and he was singing to it and talking to it, but the baby wouldn’t stop crying. Just kept on crying and crying and crying.

So Crow was getting really annoyed, no way he could stop the baby. So Crow went out and he got his boondie – his hitting stick – and banged the little fella with the hitting stick and killed him. Then he got the baby and he put it up the back of his camp, right in the back of the gunyah. He put all the leaves around it, and a bit of bark and a kangaroo skin. He had a kangaroo skin, a cloak, so he put that over the baby. And anyway, everything was quiet then so Crow went away from his camp and started doing what he wanted to do then.

So after, when Eaglehawk came back late in the afternoon, Crow ran back into the camp and he was sitting at the doorway and he was making out he was singing to the baby. Crow’s sitting there and Eaglehawk came up to him and said “I’ve come to pick my baby up now Crow. He’s very quiet, you must have sung him to sleep”.

And Crow said, “Yeah, he’s right in the back of the gunyah there, he’s right in the back of the camp. He’s sound asleep. Don’t wake him, leave him there”. Eaglehawk said, “No, I’ll take him home now and look after him”.

So when Eaglehawk walked into the camp, the gunyah, to get his baby, he noticed that everything was really still and too still around him. So once Eaglehawk walked into the back of the camp and picked the baby up, Crow took off and he ran out and hid in the mallee, the thick scrub.

So Eaglehawk he started yelling, “My baby, Crow killed my baby”, so all his other hunters came up to him with their spears and he said, “Go after him. Chase him into the thick mallee and get him. We’ll kill him”. So they ran after Crow, but he got right into the centre of the mallee and they couldn’t find him. So Eaglehawk said, “We’ll set a light to the mallee and we’ll burn him out. He’s got to be punished for what he did to my baby”.

So they set a light to the mallee, and they went right back, away from the fire and they’re sitting right out there, waiting for all the smoke to go away. And then they saw this bird flying out of the smoke, at the end of the smoke this black bird came out. And Eaglehawk said, “That’s him. That’s Crow. He’s been punished now, his spirit turned into a black bird”.

And today, Eaglehawk and Crow still carry on the fight after that. They’re birds today and they still carry on the fight. Crow will still go up to Eaglehawk’s nest and try to pick at his babies, the eyes of his babies. And in the air when Eaglehawk’s circling for food, Crow will go after him again and try to pick at him. So they still carry on the fight after what happened when they were people years ago.

— Ngiyaampaa dreamtime story about Eaglehawk and Crow

The weird Hanson sisters hand in hand. How now, you not-so-secret, white and midday hags! Your hurly-burly’s done. And I’m glad your cat is dead, you repulsive rump-fed ronyons.

You should be women and yet your beards forbid me to interpret that you are so.

Oftentimes to win us to our harm, the instruments of darkness tell us truths, win us with honest trifles, to betray’s in deepest consequence.

Nothing is but what it is not. It’s all just powdered milk for reconstituted gall.

The thriftless vaulting ambition of all those murdering ministers, and all those heat-oppressed brains leading us all down the primrose way to the everlasting bonfire.

A giant’s robes upon a dwarfish thief who uprears the universal peace and confounds all unity on earth.

As you must all know by now, I hate irony. And I hate writing about irony nearly as much as I hate irony itself. Yet it is ironic, is it not, how Shakespeare’s MacBeth, a pseudo-historical political drama based on misinformation, employs so much misinformation to caution us all against the dangers of misinformation? But given that Shakespeare wrote MacBeth shortly after the Gunpowder plot, which was supposed to have blown up Parliament, and the King of England at the time, that’s hardly surprising. Apparently the King of England at the time, a queerly superstitious Scottish dude named Jim, was also a raging tobacco-hating misogynist who believed in demons and Witchcraft. But Jim was also a staunch anti-Catholic, despite being a repressed homosexual Catholic himself, so I guess he couldn’t have been all that bad. Like most monarchs, however, he was delusional. Jim believed he was descended from the Ghost of Banquo, even though he wasn’t, which is why Shakespeare turned MacBeth into the bad guy, even though he wasn’t. The real MacBeth was in reality quite a boring ruler who never got up to much at all, neither before nor during his reign. Shakespeare wrote MacBeth at a time when witches were still being burnt at the stake and Catholics were being hanged, drawn and quartered. Of course, these witches weren’t really witches; they were just women who happened to be more knowledgeable than men. But the Catholics really were Catholics. Not that I’m excusing King Jim for persecuting Catholics; I’m merely just stating a fact.

Also a fact is the fact that since writing MacBeth Shakespeare’s MacBeth has since become more MacBeth than the real MacBeth himself. Not that that’s of any great concern for the purposes of this discussion. MacBeth is a rather hollow and uninteresting character. It is the women in MacBeth who are the most interesting characters (despite being subsequently written out). On the surface, by depicting MacBeth as a murderous usurping tyrant corrupted by the pernicious wiles and thriftless ambition of evil women, it would appear Shakespeare was merely appeasing his misogynistic and superstitious royal patron, King Jim. A closer reading, however, would appear to indicate that this not the real story. Consider the fact, for instance, that the women in MacBeth are not in fact women at all. Lady MacBeth “unsexes” herself and behaves like a cock-crazed male gangster-politician, and the Weird Sisters all have beards. In keeping with the dominant recurrent theme throughout the play – that nothing is but what is not – Shakespeare forbids us to interpret that they are in fact women. Their sex becomes entirely irrelevant; it becomes what is not. Shakespeare wrote MacBeth at quite a dangerous time to speak truth to power. He could only say what he really wanted to say by disguising it behind what was expected. But given the dramatic action of the play itself, together with its overall mood of “notness”, this is not to be unexpected. Consider also the fact that the Weird Sisters never really provide MacBeth with any truly prophetic or useful information; all they ever do is incite MacBeth to violence – as does Lady MacBeth. What if MacBeth had chosen not to act on the misinformation the Weird Sisters imparted during their first meeting? What if he had chosen not to succumb to superstition and decided not to betray and murder King Duncan? The action of the play would no doubt have suffered greatly because of it. MacBeth would have become mere fact-based historical drama. Yet just not doing all that would have surly averted MacBeth’s ultimate downfall. The Weird Sisters tell MacBeth he will be king, but they don’t tell him how. MacBeth himself determines that, goaded by Lady Macbeth’s attacks on his fragile sense of manhood. Ultimately, MacBeth’s weak vacillating will and irrational fears combine with his unnatural ambition to seal his fate. MacBeth’s story isn’t much different from the story of humanity as a whole in that respect. Nor is it that much different from the fate of King Jim himself, if one cares to take into account the immediate history of the nation he ruled shortly after his death. Shakespeare was, of course, pointing to this as King Jim’s own, not the issue of Banquo.

Some may accuse me of inflecting MacBeth with a rather liberal modicum of hindsighted modern bias, yet I would counter that my interpretation is not out of keeping with the predominating theme of the play as a whole. Regardless, a more detailed examination along these lines is entirely beyond the scope of this piece – of what is, or what was merely intended to be, a pro-anti-gay fat-shaming anti-Italianate polemic. In support of this argument, however, I find it would be dispositively disadvantageous of me – not to mention entirely out of character – to omit any mention at all of the witches’ spell (Act IV, scene I). Therefore, shall I now attempt not to do so.

Of course, anyone with any training at all in the so-called Black Arts knows this so-called witches’ spell to be pure mockery. The imposition of shockingly bizarre and outlandish ingredients such as “liver of jew”, “tartar’s lips”, and a “finger of birth-strangled babe”, commingled with the archaic and colourful vernacular names for what are in fact quite common household ingredients – mustard seed, buttercup, holly leaves, moss, ginger, garlic, wolfsbane and poppy seed (to name but a few) – is more than enough to make this self-evident to all. Europeans during the 17th century may have been somewhat superstitious, but I’m sure they weren’t completely stupid.

Similarly, I have a hard time believing Shakespeare, or his audience, truly believed mousing owls kill falcons or horses eat each other, however much the natural order is supposedly perverted by overthrowing the divine rightful rule of patrilineal monarchies (which it never is). Because if a king is a tyrant, his subjects must never rebel and always endure his tyranny for their own good. That’s The True Law of Free Monarchies, as King Jim saw it. Not that King Jim didn’t have good reason to fear getting knocked off. His cousin Francis, the Lord High Admiral of Scotland, was constantly plotting against him – as too were many others. For King Jim, the irrational fear of Witchcraft (the manifestation of superstition and misogyny) was merely an expedient tool to dispense with his political enemies, while attempting to remain in power forever – much the same way it was for Shakespeare’s MacBeth. The fact that Charles I, King Jim’s successor, inherited and upheld his father’s divine rightful rule and was eventually deposed and summarily beheaded – the English monarchy collapsing shortly thereafter – sufficiently bears this out. Throughout MacBeth Shakespeare is in fact telling us the very opposite of what King Jim believed: that we must always rebel and never endure tyranny, misogyny or superstition. Not that I’m defending Catholicism (or Witchcraft), by any means. However, I must admit I do kind of wish the Gunpowder Plot had of succeeded.

Forgive me, I do apologise for ripping off Shakespeare again. I assure you that was not my original intent. I had intended to “collusitate the great principles of action” by ripping off Harriet Beecher Stowe and quoting liberally from Uncle Tom’s Cabin. But I just couldn’t detect enough direct equivalence in any of the characters – not to mention find any passages worthy of quotation – so I gave up and resorted to ripping off Shakespeare again. Yet despite my conceded literary laziness, I think you’ll all agree that this overlaboured and predictably clichéd response has demonstrated more than adequately that knowledge is not power, and neither is truth. Power is how many other like-minded gangsters you can get together with to socially engineer the truth and organise personal take-downs of anyone who attempts to expose all your lies and corruption – primarily all the “Wordsmiths” or “Masters of English” (modern-day witches) – or anyone without a business or marketing degree – because we all know they’re all born liars and trouble makers. The fascist flaming advertainment industry gangsters like G and Co. are the only tellers of truth nowadays. Everybody knows that.

But that’s usually how it goes: 10% do all the real work while the other 90%, the puffed-up over-ambitious incompetent flamers, sit around talking about it and hating on us for it. And we reward them for that. We reward the talkers, not the workers. Why is it always the least worthy who are always the most ambitious? And why is it always those who contribute the least who are always the proudest and most boastful? Because we’re always too busy doing all their work for them? The Bestowers of Grain

Plenty of everything else on the shelves but no toilet paper!

Those words came back to haunt me yesterday while browsing the predominantly empty shelves of my local supermarket, now my only point of contact with other humans, even though all the checkouts are automated. I couldn’t find rice at all yesterday. Eggs are still relatively plentiful, however rice is nowhere to be found. I cannot survive without rice, and I’m not eating any more wheat.

I went to the supermarket again today. Now there’s no wheat or toilet paper. This appears to be the current situation in every city in Australia. Australia’s becoming more and more like Venezuela every day – the whole world is. And, as I was walking back empty-handed from the supermarket, I was nearly run down by a convoy of fascist NO MANDATE trucks. I haven’t been eating well lately and I did lose concentration there for a second while crossing the street, I must admit. You see what a menace these people are? Not only do they refuse to get vaccinated, now they’re trying to starve us all to death while running us down with their vindictively unladen big rigs. I saw a few more of them on foot a few minutes later, sauntering down St Georges Terrace in their navy blue singlets with their prominent beer guts distended over their cute little khaki shorty shorts, proudly waving their imperialist racist emblems above their impeccably perm-mulleted heads, while we’re all stuck at home, hungry and isolated, working more for less with nothing on the supermarket shelves to buy anyway. I really do wish they’d go spread Covid elsewhere. There is simply no scientific basis for any of their arguments.

I should never have defected to Westralia. It’s just a smaller version of Sydney, with more mining companies.

I arrived in Perth a poor French backpacker by way of Adelaide six months ago. I couldn’t afford to buy any food, so I went and begged for alms at that Indian restaurant by the Swan river. They provide free meals for the homeless, if you ask politely. I may have to go back there pretty soon. But what if they’re all out of rice there too? I won’t mention the name of the restaurant. I don’t do free ads (unless it’s for Hyundai or Subaru, or McDonald’s). However, I will tell you that the restaurant’s name, in Hindi, translates as “The Bestowers of Grain”. Appropriate, no?

Westralia needs far more Bestowers of Grain and way less NO MANDATE anti-vaxxing far-right trucker fuckwits, I believe. I know most Westralians don’t agree with me on that one. Most Westralians are far more afraid of French backpackers than they are of far-right mass-murdering truck drivers. I’ve always found this rather difficult to comprehend, since I’m pretty sure far-right mass-murdering truck drivers cause way more harm than French backpackers. One need merely take note of all the blood splatter patterns and dead animals by the sides of our national highways to know as much.

I assure you I have nothing personal against truck drivers – other than for all the animals they kill and all the Covid they spread, and the fact that I was once propositioned by one of them when I was 10 years old (but I won’t go into any of that here). I just don’t see truck driving as a valid profession with any kind of future. Why are we still using Covid-infected human-operated diesel-powered small-load vehicles to move containers around anyway? And why are we needlessly slaughtering so much native fauna in the process? Can’t we figure out a way to move things around without killing everything?

But you can’t reason with a mob of anti-vaxxing far-right peasants. They’ve got ignorance, faceporn and freedom on their side. I’m not dying for their brand of “freedom”. Deport them all back to Sydney. They even refuse to wear masks. They’ll wear those stupid biker gang shades alright, but they’re just way too cool to wear a mask.

What if you jackknife your big rig and get your dick caught in a ventilation shaft and they can’t stop the bleeding because all the ambulances, doctors and nurses are too busy attending to Covid patients? You ever think of that? No, because you’re stupid selfish peasants.

I don’t trust big pharma or small government either, but this is science, not money or politics. But then I’m no proponent of extreme special lockdown operations either. I suppose it could be worse. Glad I’m not in Shanghai right now. You see? This is exactly why we need a world government. We can’t leave this kind of thing up to the personally motivated benighted peasantry in future.

Toilet paper I can live without, but I cannot survive without rice, and I’m not eating any more wheat.

Update: The Bestowers of Grain have since closed. They ran out of rice, and wheat.

Perth, Westralia, 2022

How to Signify Nothing

A how-to on how to succeed in the misinformation technology industry without having to do any actual work

Introduction

As we all know, the world is coming to an end. The big powerful men with all the money in the world see no hope for humanity, therefore nor should you. Make the most of it while it lasts, because it’s not going to last for much longer – that seems to be the prevailing ethos amongst most of them. That may seem a rather cynical and pessimistic world view, yet it is the most pragmatic one. And the big powerful men with all the money, the smartest and worthiest people on the planet, are nothing if not pragmatic. But they’ll all be fine. They won’t suffer. They’ll all be living happily forever in their 3-D virtual reality worlds projected into space from their soon-to-be-completed PMC bases on the dark side of the moon, while the rest of us here back on Earth either burn or drown to death. And you’ll all burn and drown happily, won’t you? Because you all love other people’s money more than you do anything else, even more than your own lives, or those of your children. But I’m sure I don’t need to tell you that. What I do need to tell you, however, is how to become one of these big powerful rich men. Since having shitloads of money is the only way to survive the end of the world, you all want shitloads of money – but without having to do any actual work. That is natural. I don’t blame you for that. If I had anything to live for, I’d want exactly the same thing. Yet the fact is I do not. Unlike many of my contemporaries suffering under similar circumstances, however, that doesn’t mean I’m willing to just stand by and watch you all die – even though that’s exactly what’s going to happen. That is why I have written this how-to. For as we all know, the only way to make a lot of money quickly and easily these days is in the misinformation technology industry, and the only way to do that (other than by investing wisely in Bitcoin) is to own your own misinformation technology company. What follows then is a list of practical recommendations on how to successfully manage your own misinformation technology company, while doing absolutely nothing – how to do sweet fuck all and amass an obscene amount of wealth by showing off your indolence and incompetence as loudly and extravagantly as you are able – to sit back and merely signify and profit from it tremendously. Because as we all know, the secret to success in the misinformation technology industry, just as in politics, is contingent upon producing as much sound and fury as possible while signifying nothing.


So How to Signify Nothing?

  • Co-opt terms like agile and repurpose them as self-promotional micromanagement time-wasting exercises, thereby prolonging the build phase of projects for as long as possible. Gotta keep the war game profiteering going forever.

  • Schedule daily sit-down “stand-up” meetings (micromanagement status reporting sessions) as early in the morning as possible, before anyone has had time to wake up and reflect upon or analyse what they were doing the day before, let alone what they plan to do that day, which often changes throughout the day.

  • When meeting with your clients, always begin by saying “Hello, my pretties!” with as camp an accent as you can muster. And always play the role of the autocratic demagogue but disguise it with 80s game show host humour (and obscure references to inane and crass noughties television dramas such as Gossip Girls) while treating your clients like their your low-level dumb-arse shit-kicking employees. Make your client think they work for you, not the other way round.

  • Never let any developers speak during meetings, or at any time – unless they’re weak-willed sausage roll-eating Yes men.

  • Spend more time participating in as many meetings as possible and talking out of your arse than you do getting any real work done. And end every meeting with “Fly, my pretties! Fly!” – just to make it more than obvious you’re a consummate fuckwit.

  • Constantly re-enforce the value of needless and endlessly reiterative verbal communication regarding non-work-related matters over the need for producing any working code. And if anyone disagrees with this methodology, silence them by making lighthearted sadistic comments about any personal trauma they’ve suffered in the past. That always works.

  • Even if you don’t have the answer, always pretend that you do. Always say Yes to everything and casually dismiss any and all legitimate concerns or pertinent objections. Everything is easy and already “done”; and if it isn’t (which it never is), you can always hire some impoverished offshore junior developers to smash it together for you for $23 an hour – or just throw it up on faceporn or x-twatter.

  • Make personally demeaning comments about your clients behind their backs as often as you are able, while remaining totally oblivious as to how those comments are finding their way back to your clients.

  • Learn nothing about the technology used in the project itself and instead invent your own pseudo-terminology and convoluted and contradictory concepts no one else understands, and nor do you.

  • Patronise your clients endlessly by demonstrating to them how kanban boards work, over and over again.

  • If you ever have any problems with non-technical technical project mismanagers mismanaging technical projects straight into the grave, just hire two more non-technical technical project mismanagers.

  • In all written communications, always ensure you contradict yourself endlessly while confusing your client into a state of bewildered resignation by inundating them with a plethora of ambiguous terms, illogical phrases and incomplete reiterative sentences that never make sufficiently relevant or intelligible the thing which you are attempting to communicate – of which you are not, etc...

  • Charge three times as much for hosting as everyone else and run Apache 2.4.49 and PHP 7.1.0; and if the client points this out to you, flatly deny it and then charge three times as much while claiming you make no money at all from hosting. And then downgrade to Apache 2.4.41 and PHP 7.0.

  • Redesign the menu over and over again, even it doesn’t need to be redesigned, which it never does; and take over six months to do it, but never complete it.

  • Only ever hire people more incompetent than yourself, thereby ensuring your own incompetence is overshadowed by them being even more incompetent.

  • If any of your clients begin to discover just how incompetent and full of shit you are, retreat back to a passive aggressive defensive position and double up on all the personal attacks. If you can’t disguise your uselessness any other way, make it all personal or pseudo-political.

  • Pay everyone you mismanage less than a third of what you pay yourself and get them to do all the real work, which they never do.

  • Grease as many of you client’s palms as often as you can, especially those who award contracts. Everyone loves a big tipper. Then you can also use them as personal hit boys to take out any dissenters who can’t be greased.

  • Take over three months to do critical software updates, but never get around to deploying them.

  • When planning for the migration of legacy data, totally ignore the existing architecture and tell your client everything will now be handled by a random selection of never to be fully defined “taxonomies” invented by Johannes Gutenberg.

  • Whichever platform you’re designing for, disparage the fuck out of it while claiming you could build something so much better. But never actually build anything, better or otherwise.

  • Charge your client $25,000 a pop for writing up incomplete high-level functional requirements for standard functionality that has already been built by others. And always keep changing the requirements so the client can never sign off on them.

  • Never ever under any circumstances write or speak about any technical requirements. But if you absolutely must, get a loud-talking graphic designer to do it for you in a Microsoft Fucking Teams meeting towards what should be the end of the build phase – which in fact never ends.

  • When your client finally cracks and starts drinking heavily and cursing all of humanity out loud, tell everyone they’re being needlessly contentious or hostile and that they have mental health issues and need to be put out of their misery by a neofascist corporate hit squad.

  • Eat lots of sausage rolls and watch endless re-runs of Gossip Girls.

That’s about it really. Follow each and every one of these recommendations to the letter and you will most assuredly signify nothing, thereby winning the praise of your existing clients while securing myriad lucrative contracts from many more. I guarantee you, within six months you’ll be able to afford your very own rocket ship to the moon.

Marrakesh, Morocco, 1996

Japan

Sarah doesn’t love me, and Japan wasn’t as fantastical as I thought it would be. But at least now all my dreams have been shattered.

As usual, I didn’t plan at all for this trip. I stayed up all night working. I only got about two hours sleep. Luckily, I booked an Uber the night before, since there were no seats left on the bus. My Uber driver called me at 4AM. I awoke, hastily packed a few necessities – my computer, razor, toothbrush and toothpaste – and rushed downstairs.

Appropriately, my Uber driver was a Saudi “ex”-NSA agent by way of Hamilton. He asked me where I was going. I told him Japan. He told me has a “business in Japan”. I didn’t bother to ask what kind of business. He then kept asking me how much for everything.

“How much you pay for flight? How much you pay for hotel? How much you pay for taxi?”

Perhaps because I’ve always been told how expensive it is in Japan, my Uber driver’s “How much you pay?” voice became internalised throughout my entire trip. I would always hear it in my head immediately after making any kind of purchase. Furthermore, I somehow came to associate this voice with a vision of Daikokuten, the Japanese god of wealth; which, coincidentally, my Saudi “ex”-NSA agent Uber driver did very much resemble – a short portly gentleman in his mid-40s with a broad face and a bright smile, wearing a black cap, carrying a hessian sack over his shoulder and holding a large wooden mallet. He would always appear to me seated cross-legged on the floor surrounded by a family of scurrying rats. In keeping with paracusian literary tradition, I shall therefore refer to this voice, whenever it does become audible (quite often), as “a voice from below”.

Hamilton to Auckland airport is a distance of about 120 kilometres. How much I pay for the Uber ride? $350. I think it would have been less expensive to fly. Oh well, at least I didn’t get Khashoggied (yet).

Since I’m keeping with tradition, the necessary countervocal accompaniment to “a voice from below” is, of course, “a voice from above”. This higher voice presented itself to me, naturally, as the voice of Amaterasu, the goddess of the sun in the Shinto religion. She appeared to me in the air, naturally, dressed in a sumptuous red and white kimono, holding a Samurai sword in one hand and in the other a bright shinning orb, the blinding radiance of which making it impossible to discern her face. Her voice sounded like Sarah’s, only a thousand times more ethereal. She would always appear and offer wise words of encouragement or sound advice when something unfortunate happened to me, or whenever I became discouraged or annoyed. A prime example of which now follows:

A voice from above: Colgate is not the only brand of toothpaste in the world.

They confiscated my Colgate toothpaste at Auckland airport. I accidentally left my old crack pipe in my backpack. They let that go through, but they confiscated my Colgate toothpaste because it was 10g over the allowed limit of 100gs for contained liquids, even though it was half empty.

Back in the Megalopolis.

First night in Japan. I’m staying in the udon district, Kagurazaka, which also just happens to be the French geisha district. I would have stayed in the soba district but there isn’t one, as far as I know. Back during the Edo period the Edo Castle moat ran adjacent to Kagurazaka, which was quickly and easily traversable via the Ushigome bridge. Kagurazaka therefore became a renowned geisha hotspot. Then the French invaded – with udon, apparently. I didn’t know all this before deciding to stay in Kagurazaka. I only knew it was supposedly the udon district. Never believe anything you read on booking.com. And since udon is “The Queen of Noodles”, I thought it more than appropriate to stay at a hotel located in this area.

Kagurazaka-dori, the main street of Kagurazaka, is truly gorgeous – as too are many of the less conspicuous side streets. Unlike most areas in Tokyo, and despite all the upscale French udon restaurants, Kagurazaka still manages to retain at least some of its traditional Edo period charm.

So here I am at the Udon Hotel. No French geishas, or udon. Quite a nice hotel and much bigger than I expected. Nice big TV too. I’m watching the Queen “movie” (the rock group) dubbed in Japanese. First day in Japan. First order of business: I had to buy a new jūden-ki (charger) for my computer. I left that at home too. So I took a walk over to Akihabara. (Here I met my contact and we exchanged keys.) Here I met an electronics sales assistant originally from Nepal – but not by way of Redmond, Washington, and his name wasn’t Anal. (I should explain that I was recently stalked in the workplace back in Australia by a Nepalesean corporate saboteur by way of Redmond, Washington, named Anal.) I didn’t ask his name. However, the chances of his name also being Anal, given I’ve met so few people from Nepal before – not to mention the comparative rarity of the name Anal itself, one would hope – leads me to assume that his name was in all probability not Anal. It should come as no surprise then that I refer to him as NotAnal. I spoke to NotAnal in Japanese – and he understood me! Amazing. The first person I spoke Japanese to in Japan was a man from Nepal, not named Anal (I assume). Perfect. But although NotAnal understood me, he had no idea what kind of jūden-ki I required. He therefore led me over to the sales desk to speak with his colleague, Robot Girl. I call her Robot Girl because her movements and mannerisms were so precise and perfectly robotic, and also because she seemed entirely incapable of forming any form of natural facial expression. I began to wonder if she were really human and not one of those AI-enhanced Korean robotic sales assistants. She was wearing a mask, however (as were we all), so I guess she was probably a real human. Regardless, I fell in love with her instantly. But Robot Girl, too, had no idea what kind of jūden-ki I required. She therefore called in Mole Man. Mole Man was the sales manager on duty that day. I call him Mole Man simply because he had a very large and prominent mole located just above his left temple. It was truly an impressive mole; a mole that spoke authority – authority conferred through knowledge and experience, not ego or pride. With NotAnal serving as translator, Mole Man asked me what voltage, wattage and amperage I required. Chargers and power supplies come in a wide variety of configurations and choosing the wrong configuration can severely shorten the life of your battery, or even cause damage to some of your electronic components. I told him I was previously using a genuine HP Pavilion 90W AC adaptor. After taking a look at my computer, Mole Man recommended I switch to using an aftermarket 65W power supply and a 65W USB-C to USB-C cable, which was significantly less expensive than a genuine HP replacement and which I could also use to charge my other devices. He cautioned me that a 90W adaptor using the standard 4.5mm AC port was perhaps charging the battery too fast and that over time this could negatively impact its longevity. I quickly acquiesced and chose to purchase the products Mole Man recommended. How could I not? Mole Man knew his electronics – his amperes from his watts – and NotAnal and Robot Girl respected and listened carefully to Mole Man for that very reason, as did I.

And before you ask, about ¥5,000 all up.

With my jūden-ki all sorted, and since I’d forgotten to bring vape juice as well, I took a walk around Akihabara to see if I could score some of those notoriously deadly cheap black market disposable nicotine vapes (made in China). While doing so I kept stopping to look at vintage cameras. I hate cameras. Why do I keep doing that? I’m not going to start taking black-and-white pictures of old dogs in the street. I’m just not, I swear.

I didn’t find any vaping products. Combustible big tobacco products are readily available everywhere in Japan – and for about one-tenth the cost than in New Zealand – but the sale and use of vaping products is prohibited. I did, however, buy a new Bluetooth mouse: the Elecom M-BY11BR (made in China).

All convenience stores should be Japanese convenience stores. You can live out of convenience stores here (the larger ones) and still eat fairly well, and not get fat.

Just remember that there’s no Colgate toothpaste in any of the convenience stores here in Japan – anywhere in Japan in fact. Colgate toothpaste is illegal in Japan. So I bought some Lion Nonio medicated clear mint herbal toothpaste instead.

I haven’t eaten at any restaurants yet. I’ve been living out of convenience stores. I have to make up for that replacement JRail pass somehow. Yes, I do know what I’m missing. But it’s just as well. There was a U.S. food festival going on in Kyoto. Just my luck. Not that I don’t enjoy a nice big triple cheeseburger every so often, every other month or so. But I didn’t come to Kyoto for genetically modified American beef, ultra-processed orange cheese, Texas BBQ corn syrup sauce and milkshakes. I’m sure there are a lot of good restaurants in Kyoto, and I’ve walked past a few that looked quite promising. But sadly, I haven’t seen one yet capable of compelling my sullen disinterested patronage. I’m far too depressed to eat anyway and I didn’t come here for the food.

I haven’t seen any geisha yet either, except for Korean tourists dressed up like geisha. They like to take selfies of themselves as they stroll about leisurely beside the disused railway tracks. Not that I came to Kyoto for the geisha either. They’re all extinct in the wild now, so I’m told.

The U.S. military wanted to target it with a nuke. Some senior U.S. military official had a good time on his honeymoon in Kyoto – as did many of his colleagues after him – so they decided to hit Hiroshima instead. I haven’t been to Hiroshima yet. I’ll therefore refrain, for now, from questioning the reasoning behind that decision.

Kyoto is reputedly more arty and touristy than Tokyo, which is why I didn’t feel nearly so guilty about smoking kale on the street here – which I just did, behind the Imperial Palace. I never graduated. There was still a little bit of non-combusted kale left in my crack pipe. I unknowingly smuggled “drugs” into the country! ごめん. My sincerest apologies.

It was a beautiful spring day. I followed Ghoulgle maps along the disused railway tracks to a stone-paved canal flowing fast with crystal clear water. Blossomless cherry trees lined the banks of the canal. I followed the canal up the mountainside to a Shinto temple. The temple itself looked kind of crappy inside so I didn’t go in. There was, however, a rather pretty tsukiyama rock garden with a wishing pond at its centre. I threw a coin in. I wished for a good haircut.

A voice from below: How much you throw in?

I walked back the way I came. ¥500. I passed through the longest shopping arcade I’ve ever seen in my life. It must have stretched on for at least six kilometres. Most of the shops were already closed. But I did stop by one shop to buy a tan hat (made in China) and some instant noodles. ¥3,500 total. Then I went back to my hotel room and watched some more Japanese commercial television. It was a show about food – mochi, I believe.

I know, I’d have a much better time in Kyoto if I weren’t so depressed all the time. I blame all those honeymooning couples. And this city does still retain at least some small vestiges of its traditional Japanese “arty” past. But there’s no way I’m dining out alone together here, and particularly not in Gion. I’m now in Osaka.

I feel like an orphaned child having to learn the basics of life from scratch again all on my own. It took me a whole day just to figure out how the rail system works and navigate my way around some of the more massive train stations. Some of them are like entire underground cities. They have everything you could ever need down there: restaurants, cafes, supermarkets, speciality stores, barbers, salons, Pokemon trading card vending machines, etc. And the takeaway sushi is usually inexpensive and of decent quality &nfdash; and not one piece of avocado! You could live your whole life underground and never see the light of day. But perhaps that won’t be such a bad thing in future the way things are headed. Suits me just fine. I don’t much care for sunlight and I write better on trains. Conversely, I’ve noticed I get a lot more work done from hotels. Not that I should be working anyway. I’m supposed to be on leave. No more working from now on. And I’m certainly never again attempting a web platform upgrade on the Shinkansen – or the “Bullet Train”, as the English still like to call it, even though no one else calls it that. Bullets travel at an average speed of 2,800km/h; the Shinkansen only does about 300km/h. Regardless, the Japan Railways WiFi is for the most part as fast and reliable as their trains. Yet there were some odd moments when the connection did drop out for a few seconds. I shouldn’t be working anyway.

I never seem to get much reading done either when I travel by train. There’s far too many distractions – the scenery, for one. Not that there’s too much of any great interest to see between the major population centres, other than your standard prefabricated forms of rural-suburban-industrial infrastructure. Only here they’re a lot more compact and neater. Japan also has the neatest and tidiest construction sites I think I’ve ever seen. Everything looks so well-organised and efficient, even the rural-suburban-industrial areas. While staring out the window, I began to wonder what it must be like to reside in one those areas; to live and die all alone in one of those tiny little apartments in one of those soulless beige-grey concrete oblong apartment buildings right beside the railway line. I tried to imagine what it’s like to be truly anonymous in Japan. Probably not as romantic as I imagine it. But at least I’d get to see the Shinkansen zoom past at 300km/h every so often, at no less than ten metres from my bedroom window.

I also spotted the Tamiya factory from the train window – in Oshika, Shizuoka city – on the way from Tokyo. It brought back fond memories of my preemptive drone experiment days when I was a kid. I was obsessed with radio-controlled cars and planes back then (for about 18 months or so). Back then batteries were still too heavy. You could only maintain sustained powered flight or drive time for about five minutes, and no vertical flight or hovering. Nickel-cadmium batteries were in use in those days. Lithium-ion polymer batteries were still a few years off. I always used to read all the hobby magazines and try to stay abreast of all the latest RC technology advances coming out of Japan. I think that’s where my fascination for Japan first began. I thought about getting off at Shin-Shizuoka Station and checking out the factory. I’m glad I didn’t. I later found out that what I saw from the train window is no longer the Tamiya factory. Turns out it was just a sign for their head office. All the manufacturing has since moved to Antipolo City, Philippines.

I decided to rent a car in Osaka. I wanted to take a drive around for a while and then head over to Kobe to see the Osaka Hankyu Railway Kobe Main Line trains. Renting a car in Japan involves almost as much paperwork and bureaucracy as it does to rent an apartment in Australia. I’m surprised they didn’t ask to see my bank statements for the past five years or request a DNA sample. The car was a Nissan Note, which was easy enough to drive. But just in case I ran into any difficulties, the car also came with two massive binders containing the operation and compliance manuals (almost as large as the car itself and printed in Japanese only) which kept falling out of their storage compartments as I drove. Besides that, driving in Osaka is pretty straight forward, and people here are usually more courteous and safer drivers than in most other countries I’ve driven in. Still, I had no idea where I was going most of the time.

Stupid old homeless cunt in a rental driving around all over Osaka aimlessly, spending more on tolls than he did to rent the car. The ETC tag (Electronic Toll Crap) wasn’t working, which meant I had to stop and pay cash. I also kept getting in the wrong lane when going through the tollway. One of the tollway guys had to run over with one of those little red flags to collect the cash from me and open the boom gate manually. I must have done it about three or four times. I swear, it wasn’t deliberate. But no one complained or got angry with me.

A voice from below: How much you pay for tolls?

More than I paid to rent the car.

I forgot to ask about the tolls and the ETC thing when I rented the car. I really should have taken some Japanese language classes before arriving.

A voice from above: Yes, you should have.

I can sing the theme song to Galaxy Express 999 and say thank you well enough but that’s about it. Also, I brought the car back on time, and with a full tank of fuel, but I couldn’t find the car rental company at Shin-Osaka. I circled the station three times, which took about two hours, tried a few alternate routes and cursed all of humanity out loud while doing so, yet all to no avail – and no it wasn’t on Ghoulgle maps (in English). Finding the entrance to the car rental area proved to be no less difficult a task than the Siege of Osaka (1615) when the Tokugawa shogunate stormed Osaka Castle and overthrew the Toyotomi clan. Finally I gave up, parked in a private carpark and checked into a nearby Comfort Hotel. I called the car rental company the next day and they came and picked the car up. As soon as you start living outside your routine on the spur of the moment and throwing away your old pants you start making stupid mistakes like that.

A voice from below: How much you pay for lost parking ticket?

They told me it’s ¥100,000 if you lose the ticket. I think they were just fucking with me. Osakans are quite the comedians. They haven’t charged my credit card yet. If they do, I may have to abort my mission.

But at least I got to see the Osaka Hankyu Railway Kobe Main Line trains. I saw the Hankyu 8000, 7000 and the 6000 series. I’m not really a hardcore railway geek, but there is something special about these particular trains. It must be their bold all-burgundy livery together with that suave yet simple design, and the fact that they’re used every day by the public – they’re not just weekend boutique trains – yet still retain much of their genuine historic mystique. Still, I’m never renting a car again unless I absolutely must (always say that). It takes longer to get around here in a car anyway.

I finally got a haircut today, in Shinsaibashi on Midōsuji Avenue, at the most exclusive-looking hair salon I’ve ever seen in my life. I just marched straight in off the street and told them I needed a haircut. They looked at me like I just stepped out of the jungle of north-east Burma. And when I sat down in the barber chair and removed my tan hat and mask, the hairstylist gasped aloud in genuine horror. I wasn’t at all offended by that, however. I was more relieved they didn’t ask me to leave as soon as I walked in. Offence was given, on my part, however, when I used what I thought was a hand towel to clean my hands. It wasn’t a hand towel; it was a head towel. They use damp towels instead of those hair spray mister things to wet your hair here. The hairstylist gasped aloud again in genuine horror upon discovering my monstrous faux pas of Japanese coiffeurist etiquette. A few moments later a young woman appeared with a fresh set of damp towels. She then began gently massaging my head with them, until what remains of my unruly and overgrown head of hair was sufficiently moist and more manageable. About ten minutes later the hairstylist reappeared and proceeded to cut my hair. The haircut itself was okay, I guess. And thankfully it took less than five minutes. But on second thought, I probably should have just gone to one of those barbers at the train station.

A voice from below: How much you pay for Shinsaibashi wet head massage?

That’s not important right now. What is important, and which I was also about to mention, is that I keep speaking Spanish instead of Japanese. I did it to the hairstylist too. I kept saying gracias and si instead of arigato gozaimasuuu and hai. Arigato gozaimasuuu is too long anyway. I’m usually gone by the gozaimasuuu part. Apparently, stretching out the sound of some Japanese words makes them sound more polite and meaningful, even though it’s the same word and means the same thing. Abrupt is rude – unless it’s hai. I prefer the word efficient. In any case, I’m only going to say domo or “thanks” from now on. And no one says konichiwa here, unless they’re old or work for NHK. In future, I’m only going to use “hello” for greetings. That’s all the Japanese you really need to know, and Ghoulgle Translate for more complex stuff. And if someone speaks Japanese to me in more than a few words, I’ll simply have to assume they’re just being a dick.

A voice from above: I’ll pretend you didn’t just say that, for now.

I also went clothes shopping in Shinsaibashi, an activity to which I’m almost averse as getting haircuts. I needed some new pants and a few more t-shirts. They only had sexy skintight black leggings at Uniqlo, so I bought a pair of black pants from GU.

A voice from below: How much you pay for nonsexy GU black pants?

¥2,900.

Now, and after the haircut, all I have to do is lose the tan hat, exchange the hoodie for a black blazer and I can pretty much get in anywhere. GU is even less expensive than Uniqlo, and of fairly decent quality too. So if I see any more “Aussie” or “Kiwi” tourists wearing dirty grey tracky dacks, I’m going to pants them. Grey tracky dacks are illegal in Japan (illegal to wear outside the home), and since there is so much affordable quality clothing here, there’s simply no excuse to be wearing dirty grey tracky dacks (even in the home).

Although Osaka has a population of around 19 million, it’s generally more homely and relaxed than Tokyo. Moreover, Osaka has a lot more birds than Tokyo (crows and pigeons mostly). Osaka also has more waterways and bridges than most other cities – especially around Dōtonbori, which is known as the Venetian Times Square of Japan. I spent a bit of time wandering around Dōtonbori today. There’s so many restaurants and street food vendors here. Osaka is renowned for its food culture (and overeating). Still, I didn’t get to sample any of it. Still too depressed. I bought some more instant noodles and three Fuji apples to stave off scurvy, then went back to my hotel and watched some more Japanese commercial television.

Some of these hotel rooms are so small I keep walking into things and injuring myself. I can’t believe I stayed in my hotel room all last night watching Japanese commercial television. How depressing. I’ve seen hardly anything of Osaka. I didn’t even get to see Osaka Castle, or any of the galleries or museums.

And yet I must note that I was afforded the unique privilege of seeing a tall skinny Japanese-Korean dude with spiky anime character hair dressed all in black, wearing skintight black leggings with no underwear (over-accentuating the positive) strutting around Osaka-Shin station like he owned the place. I think he thought I cut in front of him in line while waiting to buy a ticket. So he started doing his level best to try to physically intimidate me with a series of weird-arse close-proximity strutting gestures, while giving me his level best sexy anime character stink-eye. I wasn’t even standing in line; I was checking the train timetable on my personal surveillance device. But since he took that attitude, I pretended I was in line for as long as possible just to annoy him, while he continued to strut around menacingly in those sexy skintight black leggings – until I got to the ticketing window. Then I quit the line and went and boarded my train.

Don’t worry, I’m not going to do the whole clichéd “weird Japan” thing from a ignorant Westerner’s perspective, I’m just not. In any case, that weird-arse strutting sexy skintight black leggings-wearing spiky-haired anime character dude was the only weird thing I’ve seen so far. Japan really isn’t that weird. I’ve seen a lot weirder elsewhere. Even Japanese commercial television isn’t as weird as I thought it would be.

As mentioned previously, I spent my last night in Osaka all alone watching Japanese commercial television (on mute), while eating instant noodles and Fuji apples, and while constantly reproaching myself for forgetting to bring vape juice. They put me in an industrial-soundproofed ground-floor room right next to the railway line. A train went past at least every five minutes, at no less than ten metres from my hotel room window. But I couldn’t hear a thing. Nor did I feel anything. I almost felt as if I were truly anonymous.

I can’t believe I unknowingly remembered to smuggle marijuana into the country but forgot to smuggle in some vape juice. So I’ve started smoking Parliament Lights again (“refinement in smoking”).
