I’m still not sure why I decided to get off the train in Sendai. I wanted to smoke a cigarette, but I suspect that wasn’t the main reason.

Sendai, City of Trees. Hmmm. From what I’ve seen, I doubt any city in Japan could claim that title. Not many cities anywhere else could either.

They are nice trees, I must admit. But a few dozen Zelkova trees lining Jozenji-dori avenue does not a City of Trees make. Nonetheless, they are nice trees, and they do sometimes provide a very useful public service. In Japanese folklore Zelkova trees are known as “the protectors of the people”, and it is true they did protect more than a few people during the tsunami that followed the 2011 Tohoku earthquake. People all over Sendai clung to them to escape the surging black waves of devastation. The atavistic urge to hide under the leaves of trees never leaves us, so it would seem. Sendai was the largest city closest to the epicentre – only 130 kilometres.

I didn’t see any cherry blossoms in Sendai. But I did see a nice bronze statue of a large-breasted naked lady drying her hair under the Zelkova trees. At least I learned something about Zelkova trees and got to see some well-sculptured big bronze boobs. And I also learned that the word tsunami originated in this part of Japan, in 1896 after the Sanriku earthquake.

Sendai is a modern city in harmony with nature, so they say. I don’t know about that. But I must say it is a nice city. They also have some very good ramen restaurants. In fact, I ate some of the finest ramen I’ve ever eaten in my life in Sendai. I ordered the braised pork with the thicker noodles – midway between udon and soba. A little too firm for my liking but still very good. I wasn’t even looking for ramen. I just passed by this place by chance, and it didn’t even look that good from the outside. Always the way. It must have been the intoxicating aroma of braised pork broth wafting out into the street. And no I’m not going to tell you where it is. Do your own research.

Sendai, a city in harmony with the aroma of braised pork broth, and a few dozen Zelkova trees.

I liked Sendai so much I decided to stay the night. I’m staying at the Sendai Washington Hotel, right across the road from the Japan Railways Building. I can see straight into their offices from my hotel room window. It’s 8PM on a Friday and people are still working – as too am I. I wonder what they’re working on. Issuing replacement lost JRail passes perhaps?


*

Northern Japan reminds me a little of Southern Aotearoa, only more Japanese people and a lot less cows. Similar landscape and weather, same 1980s-era infrastructure, same general sense of economic malaise. It does snow a lot more here, however. In fact, Aomori City is reputedly the snowiest city in the world. But thankfully it’s now Spring (kind of), so it wasn’t snowing when I arrived. I don’t like snow.

I arrived to the sound of the worst played best-sounding street piano I’ve ever heard in my life. They have a brand new full-size white Yamaha grand piano at Shin-Aomori Station, and an endless selection of musically inclined tone deaf rail commuters willing to play it. At least it wasn’t snowing.

On my first day in Aomori City I visited the Nebuta Museum WA-RASSE, which is conveniently and centrally located right next door to the train station. The museum itself is a distinctive piece of modern architectural art in itself, the exterior of which is made up of hundreds of red steel ribbons parted like curtains at its entrances, which enticingly yet disappointingly seem to promise so much more than than the interior contains. The Nebuta Museum WA-RASSE houses a vast collection of enormous brightly coloured papier-mâché floats depicting kabuki actors, various types of gods, sumo wrestlers, and historical or mythical figures from Japanese or Chinese culture. For a few days in August these floats are dragged out, lit up and paraded around the streets of Aomori City in what is known as the Aomori Nebuta Matsuri. Apparently it’s one of the biggest festivals in all of northern Japan. In addition to drawing some of the largest crowds you’d ever wish to avoid, the Aomori Nebuta Matsuri is also notorious for attracting a small group of young people known as the karasu zoku (or the “crow tribe”), who dress all in black and make a thorough nuisance of themselves by drinking large quantities of saké and throwing cherry bombs into the crowds. Incidentally, the phrase karasu zoku is borrowed from the Japanese fashion industry. It was a “full body darkening” fashion style popular during the 1980s.


The karasu zoku style is all about bold, oversized clothing. The androgynous look, as well as asymmetrical cuts, were popular. Clothes were meant to cover the body shape, not enhance it. In general, the style was inspired by the aesthetics of the British punk movement.

— j-fashion.fandom.com


Still, fashionable or not, and I’m not at all condoning their behaviour, but I think the karasu zoku are totally awesome. And I suppose that’s why there’s usually a more visible police presence here in Aomori City than most other cities in Japan. The police probably think they’re nothing but North Korean anarchists in disguise. I wonder what the karasu zoku are really protesting against. I never did find out. Is it all the economic malaise? Or are they just annoyed by all the bright gaudy colours, large crowds and excessive noise? Or are they merely objecting to the fact that the most appropriate and centrally located modern art building in town is currently being used as a papier-mâché lantern storehouse?

On my second day in Aomori City I decided to visit the Aomori Museum of Art, which is not conveniently or centrally located, near anything. I had to take a half-hour taxi ride just to get there. There was a Narita Tohl exhibit going on that day. Narita Tohl was a visual artist who grew up in Aomori and worked on the Ultraman television series (1966-67). Ultraman was a large masked man in a silver and orange rubber jumpsuit who liked to beat the shit out of giant goannas (Perentie giganteus). I’ve never really been much of a fan of the kyodai hero genre, or tokusatsu “movies” in general, but it was interesting seeing the early sketches of some of Narita’s rather visionary engineering design work. I kept thinking about how all this feeds back into real design a generation later. Some of the stuff he dreamed up in the late 60s resembles modern-day real hardware, particularly the aircraft.

On my third day in Aomori City there didn’t appear to be much else to do, so I caught a train out to Hirosaki.


*

I bought a ¥740 umbrella and a pair of Mickey Mouse socks in Hirosaki. I was in a hurry and couldn’t find any plain black socks.

A voice from below: How much you pay for Mickey Mouse socks?

I don’t remember, so I can’t tell you. But I can tell you that I have a spectacular view of Mount Iwaki from my hotel room window. It’s actually a dormant stratovolcano. I can also tell you that Hirosaki is supposedly one of the most spectacular cherry blossom spots in all of Japan.

Earlier, I took a walk around town. I didn’t see any cherry blossoms, but I did see two or three plum trees still in bloom. It must be all that cool air blowing down off the mountainside. Or maybe it’s just because this part of Japan is closer to the sky? It was such a nice day I planned on walking all the way to Hirosaki Castle, the seat of the Tsugaru clan. Then it started to rain – large heavy drops. It’s not supposed to rain like this until mid-June. Tsuyu rain they call it, or “plum rain”. Michizane, the ninth-century Japanese poet-bureaucrat, wrote about it.


あめの下のがるゝ人のなければや着てし濡れ衣干るよしもなき

From the heavens’ falling rain,
No one escapes,
So,
Blameless, I wear my soaking clothes
With no way to dry them.

東風吹かばにほひをこせよ梅花主なしとて春を忘るな

Should the east winds blow,
Carry me the fragrance
Of plum blossom;
And though your lord is gone,
Never forget the springtime.

— Sugawara no Michizane


Michizane wrote those lines while in exile, after having been banished by the Emperor Daigo for ripping off Du Fu, the eight-century Chinese poet-bureaucrat – and for fraternising with plum trees. But at least he still believed in Spring.

Michizane was of the Sugawara clan, not the Tsugaru clan. But you get what I mean.

Upon arriving back at my hotel, I changed out of my soaking wet clothes – into my grey tracky dacks and my new Mickey Mouse socks – sprawled out on the nice big queen-size bed (which took up the whole room) and stared out the window at Mount Iwaki for a while. I usually don’t dream these days, and when I do they’re rarely worth remembering, let alone writing about. That afternoon, however, as the sun was setting behind the mountain, I dozed off and dreamed the following:

I’m walking down the main street of a deserted small town in northern Japan. Traditional wooden houses line the street on either side. The houses are clean and well-maintained yet utterly vacant inside. It starts to rain – relentless heavy rain – and a cold hard wind begins to blow. I keep walking to the outskirts of the town, encountering no one – until I come to a broad deep river flowing fast with bright green-coloured water. Ghostly barren cherry trees line the near side of the river, while on the other side, rising out of a whirlwind of tumultuous clouds, I espy an austere stone castle atop a steep high hill. Instinctively, I know that’s where I need to be. But there doesn’t appear to be a bridge. I walk for what feels like many kilometres along the side of the river, which seems to endlessly encircle the hill, yet not one bridge do I see. Then I see an old man walking slowly towards me, hunched over, hobbling along with a crooked walking stick. I say hello and ask him how to cross the river. He doesn’t respond. He doesn’t even look at me – like I’m a ghost and he doesn’t see or hear me at all. Then, as he passes me by, I hear the sound of a woman’s voice singing. It sounds like it’s coming from the bottom of the river, calling to me. Ōkī magoi wa otōsan, she sings. I look down into the lucid green water. A large whirlpool begins to form, from the centre of which the sound of her voice grows ever louder. Then I know it’s Sarah calling me. I feel an overwhelming urge to jump straight in and drown myself in the sound.

Beyond the banal and obvious psycho-sexual-death symbolism, I’m not entirely sure how to interpret this dream. I’d read something earlier that day about carp (Cyprinidae): how their swim bladders are connected to their inner ears in what is known as the Weberian organ, giving them excellent hearing underwater; and I’d also recently learned how the original form of sushi, known as funazushi, was originally made from funa (fermented carp), and that modern-day “fast” sushi would probably not exist at all if not for the invention of soy sauce. Perhaps all that had something to do with it. Or perhaps it was merely yet another vivid reminder of the eternal torments one must necessarily endure while living an endless living death?

Or it could be that I’m just suffering from an overstimulated imagination. I have experienced quite a lot of stimulation over the last few days. I believe a sensory distillation process is required. No more input for a while – but for Tsugaru soba and shamisen, and Mount Iwaki. And no more dreaming about Sarah.


Tsugaru Soba

I finally ate soba today. I chanced upon a clandestine Tsugaru soba restaurant while exploring the outskirts of the town. Heaven noodles. No other way to describe them. Grilled dried soybean stock as the binding agent. Perfect consistency. Firm yet melt in your mouth after about 3-4 seconds. Almost no need to chew. The broth was a little too bland for my liking, but still very good. You can never have everything, even in heaven.

It always amazes me how the same dish can taste so different depending on where and how it’s made.


Tsugaru Shamisen

She was of the Tsugaru clan, I could tell instantly. I don’t know how. I’ve never been here before, or even met anyone of the Tsugaru clan before, yet I was certain of it the moment she met me at the door.

She told me to go away – politely of course. She told me I was too late for the performance that evening and that I should make a booking for the following evening – which I did.

I wasn’t nearly so nervous when she met me at the door the following evening, although I was still quite nervous. I was afraid she’d have no trouble seeing straight through to the core of my shamefully ill-mannered and uncouth nature – and my deplorable lack of Japanese language skills – and turn me away right then and there at the door, again. In my then-current fragile state of mind, and after being turned away at the door the previous evening, even one slightly admonishing gesture from her would have been enough to totally destroy me. Thankfully, that didn’t happen. She gracefully guided me to my table and patiently explained the menu to me. I ordered some sushi (no carp) and an Ahhsaaheee!

The sushi was amazingly good, considering Hirosaki is nowhere near the sea – a fresh delectable selection of just about every variety of fish imaginable (except carp). I devoured them all in under ten minutes, and the Ahhsaaheee! Then the music started.

The sound is incisive, it cuts through you whole – same as their swords, same as that cooler air blowing down off the mountainside. How three silk strings stretched across a slim piece of rosewood attached to a small square drum can make such a sound is entirely beyond me. It must be in part attributable to the plectrum, known as a bachi, which very much resembles a large plastic paint scraper. They’re not really made of plastic, of course. I later found out they’re made from tortoise shell and cost over ¥60,000. Tortoise shell as the binding agent. I may have to steal that idea. I also later found out that the word bachi is the same word for drumstick. Watching and listening to how the Tsugaru shamisen is played you can understand why. The strings are more struck than plucked.

Apparently, this vigorous and virtuosic style of shamisen playing was invented by blind beggars – stupid old visually impaired homeless cunts known as bosama – in response to the poverty that inevitably results after suffering through endless natural disasters. I may have to steal that idea as well. I think I already have. I can only play three strings at once too.

He was of the Tsugaru clan, I could tell instantly, right from the moment he took the stage. He wasn’t a blind beggar, or a stupid old homeless cunt, but he did keep his eyes closed during the whole performance and he rarely spoke. There were no lyrics, except for the occasional hup and hey to mark the chord changes – the only two words you ever really need really.

It is no mere exaggeration to say the sound cuts right through you. There is simply no more accurate way to describe the effect Tsugaru shamisen has on one’s senses. And even now, as I listen to a 1970s recording of the great Tsugaru shamisen master, Takahashi Chikuzan, I’m still at a loss for words. Recordings don’t even come close to capturing the visceral nature of this sound, no more than I can by stringing a few inadequate words together. Tsugaru shamisen must be immediately experienced by all the senses, not just heard.

And that’s not just my personal opinion. There was a group of skiing tourists from Okinawa at the table over from me, whom I could plainly see were similarly affected. I even overheard one of their party outwardly express disappointment that the music only lasted an hour and her earnest desire to go out dancing afterwards (wildly, I presume). I wish I could have joined them.


Being with friends and dancing is the secret to life.

— a woman from Okinawa

Knowing how to dance and who your friends are, if you have any, is important too.

— some stupid old homeless cunt

The round of the peaks and the roaring at the centre announce that the snows are not far away.

— Yasunari Kawabata

Due to the lack of snow, GALA Yuzawa Ski Resort will be closed for the season on April 23, 2023 (Sunday). Please note that due to this, the Joetsu Shinkansen between Echigo Yuzawa Station and Gala Yuzawa Station will be suspended.

— Japan Railways announcement


Mount Iwaki

An old man on the street just gave me a brochure with a spectacular picture of Mount Iwaki on the cover (taken twenty years ago). I thought it was some kind of tourist information thing, so I accepted it and thanked him kindly. But upon translating the text I quickly discovered it was merely an advertisement for Buddhism. All the world’s problems would be solved instantly if people would only believe in Buddha, so the copy read. What any of that has to do with Mount Iwaki I’m still at a loss to interpret. It is estimated that 20 years from now Mount Iwaki will be without snow all year round, whether you believe in Buddha or not.

Imported religions are a lot like imported beer. I don’t need no imported religions. I have Ahhsaaheee!

A voice from above: Indeed.


Hirosaki Castle

Last day in Hirosaki. Today I visited Hirosaki Castle, the seat of the Tsugaru clan. There’s a cherry-tree lined moat around the castle grounds. The moat is inhabited by a good deal of large brown carp. I didn’t see any cherry blossoms here either. But I did see a very beautiful woman in a long white dress near the entrance to the castle. She was standing by the moat staring down into the murky green water. She clapped her hands loudly two times. The large brown carp all congregated before her. There must have been about 50 of them. They swam around in slow concentric circles, occasionally rising to the surface. They all had their eyes fixed on her, as if mesmerised. She stood there for a few seconds inspecting them carefully, then she turned suddenly and casually walked away. I could have sworn I saw her again at the Hirosaki train station as I was leaving, only this time she was wearing a long dark brown dress. I couldn’t see her face; she was wearing a mask. She gave me a long knowing look as she walked by me, which I returned as best I could. I wonder if she’s of the Tsugaru clan.


*

Back in Tokyo again. I decided to visit the National Art Centre of Tokyo, the Mori Art Museum, and the National Museum of Modern Art. Yes, I decided to take in some real Japanese culture for a change.

If ever I have my own exhibit in a modern art gallery (which I never will), I would like it to be titled, Experiments in Deconstructed De facto Solidarity: Mastering the breaking of rectangular abstractions of impure necessity after looking at too much so-called modern art.

I learned a new Japanese word today, at the National Art Centre of Tokyo: 歌垣 (utagaki). And I saw some pictures I’ve never seen before, by Ikkō Narahara.

She looks exactly how I feel after looking at too much modern art. Why does she look so unwell? And what does she have in her right hand? There were two other photographs of her, in the act of rising to her feet, above the photograph I include here, which I do not include here. Do your own research.

They also had some Paul Klee pictures, at the National Museum of Modern Art. I had no idea Paul Klee was a Japanese modern artist. I thought he was a Swiss furniture designer. He was also quite a good fiddle player, incidentally.

All Swiss furniture aside, I quite like Paul Klee. Probably because he was a musician and imbued his work with so much movement. He may not have been a Japanese modern artist, but he was a master rectangle wrangler of much polyphonic chiaroscuro – which I suppose is why the Japanese like him too. I especially like how he can’t be classified as belonging to any single “school” of art. Klee constructed his own school. He also liked to paint fish, incidentally – a few of them carp.

Some old Chinese dude just farted really loudly in the Paul Klee exhibit. Seriously, that really just happened, while I was thinking about writing that paragraph above. New Zen Buddhist meditation technique? Farting loudly in Japanese modern art galleries beside Paul Klee pictures?

The Mori Art Museum is located on the 52nd floor of the Roppongi Hills Building, where all the untaxed exceedingly wealthy people live. On a clearer day you can barely see all the way to Mount Fuji. There was a Disney animation exhibit going on. It was sold out, damn it. There was also an Architecture that Attempts to Mimic Some Aspects of Nature exhibit going on. So I saw that. Some nice ideas, but most of the designs weren’t structurally integrated into the landscape or the native ecology as a whole; still merely a rudimentary stylised mimicry of nature; “sustainability” marketing in architectural form. Nevertheless, looking out across all of Tokyo from the 52nd floor of the Roppongi Hills Building, across that endless cubist patchwork of tightly packed beige-grey concrete oblongs, I must admit their designs were infinitely more preferable to any more of those tightly packed beige-grey concrete oblongs.

I’m all galleried out now. No reasonably sentient human being can do more than three galleries in one day. To do any more results in visual sensory input overload. They usually put the best stuff at the start anyway, so just get a look at the first three pictures near the entrance then move on to the next exhibit. Most so-called modern art is vulgar, pretentious and plagiarised, the world over. Commercial designers ripping off the rare good stuff. They all end up in advertising eventually, or in prison. Suffered some political persecution in the past so they stack some reconstructed detritus up on the floor or take a selfie of their ungroomed arthouse muff and call it art. Yeah, thanks for that.

I never made it to the other galleries. I have to go back.

A voice from below: Come now, how many more pictures of ungroomed arthouse muff do you need to see?

Lots!

A voice from above: I concur. In fact, that ungroomed arthouse muff you saw at the National Museum of Modern Art – that wall-sized full-colour super glossy high definition triptych of that young Japanese woman artist (what’s her name?); her ungroomed arthouse muff the first panel, her pimply nubile backside the second, her young yet stern and care-worn face the third – I thought particularly thought provoking, if not profound. It’s quite a bold statement for a young artist to make and provokes a very important question in response: “Here’s my cunt, here’s my arse, here’s my face, in that order. How does that make you feel?”

Much the same way Hieronymus Bosch’s The Garden of Earthly Delights makes me feel. Same old, same old.

A voice from below: That’s, of course, assuming you view the triptych from left to right, in that order.

Good point.

I wonder where Sarah is right now. I wonder if she would concur with my broadly reductive generalisation regarding all so-called modern art. I’m staying in Ginza behind the Kabukiza Theatre. She could find out which hotel if she really wanted to. She’s probably not even in Tokyo. She probably left for Sydney the day after the show. She’s probably staying at the Ritz-Carlton with Mister Hairy Arms, or with that cute Italian journalist – or both, just to make a point of it.


*

I heard flutes, whistles, and the beating of drums (taiko). A large crowd had gathered outside my hotel. They carried a small golden shrine (a mikoshi) through the streets of Ginza – an intricately carved model of the real shrine plated in gold leaf with a golden bird at each corner and an even larger golden bird with long tail feathers perched at its very top (the only kind of bird life you’re likely to see or hear in this city, unless it’s a cutesiepoo cartoon character). They were preparing for Sanja Matsuri.

Matsuris are rather crowded and noisy affairs. But Shinto is a non-authoritarian animistic nature religion with much in common with Australian Aboriginal spiritual practises, so I wasn’t at all perturbed by all the noise and quite happily mingled with the crowd and joined in the procession. Western anthropologists would argue that Australian Aboriginal spiritual beliefs should more strictly be termed totemic rather than animistic, and that some Aboriginal cultural practises could be considered quite authoritarian. Whatever the case, the shared metaphysical belief that all things contain “soul” is enough for me. In fact, if ever I were forced to choose a religion it would definitely be Shintoism...if not Taoism or Zoroastrianism, or Aboism.

I’ve been here nearly two weeks now and despite not knowing anyone or speaking the language I feel right at home, if it weren’t for the lack of bird life. In fact, Tokyo is just a bigger version of Perth, with more Japanese people and no Aboriginal people, and no birds. Perhaps I’ve living been out in the sticks for too long, and perhaps I’ve been corrupted by the relative abundance of bird song still to be heard in Aotearoa, but I’d be lying if I said that didn’t that worry me. Although, I do quite enjoy the quiet here. In fact, I think Tokyo is the quietest big city I’ve ever visited – when there isn’t a matsuri going on. But I still think Japan needs more birds, and Aotearoa and Australia need more trains. Over half have undergone significant species loss, in both cases.

And yet I must admit I have violated a few social norms during my time in Japan: I drank an Ahhsaaheee! on the street (once); I smoked outside (a few times, but discreetly and I never littered); I sneezed in public (twice); I cursed out loud a few times, under my breath (that piece of glass is still stuck in my left foot); I talked on the phone (once) on the Shinkansen (you’re supposed to go to the space between the carriages); I wore grey tracky dacks (indoors); I went over the speed limit (twice) while driving through Kobe; and I disposed of some non-required luggage (no human remains) by leaving it in my vacated hotel room without informing the staff. (And I’ve obviously gone completely nuts with the parentheticals.)


*

Last day in Japan. I’ve yet to build up a tolerance to instant coffee, and I’m still waking up at 4am but nothing’s open until 11am. Stupid holiday hours. I checked out of my hotel at 10AM, walked around Ginza for an hour or so, ate a Belgian waffle with vanilla ice cream for breakfast in Ginza Sony Park, then I went to see the kabuki. I saw Kotobuki Soga no Taimen, a slow motion 17th-century vendetta play about two brothers seeking revenge for their murdered father. The lead actor wasn’t played by Tom Hanks and the script wasn’t written by Ben Stiller. There were no black people (or foreigners) and only two women. There was, however, a blackface part, or “monkey makeup” part as they call it in kabuki. Both the women were played by Japanese men, as too was the monkey makeup part. So all up there were 19 colourfully dressed Japanese men on stage, one in blackface, two in drag. I started to nod off, I must admit – not because I was bored, but because I was very tired and because of the dreamlike fantastical splendour of it all. I think the lead actor, playing Soga no Gorō, saw me nodding off. I’m not kidding. When he got to the part where he angrily throws down his saké and breaks the rectangular wooden serving tray, I could have sworn he was glaring directly at me; his eyes like two fiery Tamahagane-forged Samurai swords simultaneously perforating and searing my soul with intensely directed thrusts of carefully controlled yet for the most part wholly unmitigated pure rage.

After the play ended I caught a train back to the airport. I hate airports (transit detention centres) but I think I could live at Narita International Airport. There’s more restaurants there than in all of New Zealand. They even have a Uniqlo there. It’s all coming out of Vietnam and Bangladesh anyway.

Thankfully, I didn’t get rear-ended by a great big man-bunned Indian bitch-man this time, and nothing else untoward happen to me. But I did forget to swipe my passport when I checked in (consciously?) and customs confiscated my flask of Suntory whiskey (still three-quarters full). They also took my Swiss Army keychain pocket knife. Probably for the best. I don’t handle rejection well. The young woman from customs who relieved me of my contraband items was so undeniably charming I really didn’t mind, as too was the young woman from ANA who completed my incomplete check-in. I wonder if they’re of the Tsugaru clan.

They have WiFi on this flight! And it works! A true miracle! I’ve been waiting 23 years to use WiFi on a plane. I’m drafting this ending and committing changes at 37,000 ft above sea level. We just passed Torishima Island. But then who cares? No one is reading this. Who am I writing this for? There is no one now.

That’s where I was going to end it. I pushed that change a little too early. I planned to sleep all the way. The two seats beside me were empty.

A voice from below: How much you pay for three seats?

$20. I upgraded my seat on the Air Aotearoa website.

I didn’t dream. I awoke at 4AM (1AM local) to the sound of someone on the other side of the plane opening a bag of peanuts. Noise-cancelling headphones, my arse. I couldn’t get back to sleep. Not that I’m complaining. Three hours of real sleep on a plane is more than I was hoping for. I didn’t watch any sappy kitsch pro-rape Hollywood propaganda this time. I stared out of the window and thought of Sarah. The narrator’s closing words from the final episode of Galaxy Express 999 came back to haunt me:


Tetsuro thinks to himself that perhaps from the very beginning his journey was in fact a solitary one; that Maetel was merely a vision that propelled his youth – a vision born in the hearts of many young boys, a fleeting dream towards the future...

A future that no longer exists.

I had the seat right next to the starboard engine, looking out across the wing. It was perfectly calm – as it usually is at that altitude. There was a large full moon illuminating an endless white expanse of uniformly layered stratus clouds. It always unsettles me how the moon seems to follow you if you stare at it for long enough, especially on a plane. The engines on 787s are huge yet the wings look so slight and delicate, especially from this angle. We have to descend through all that dense cloud cover pretty soon. I hope Auckland Airport isn’t flooded again. That dude is still trying to open that bag of peanuts. I wonder if they’re taking extreme weather into account when they design these things nowadays. I hate flying as a passenger...unless it’s with Air Aotearoa.

My only complaint about Air Aotearoa: those hot pink and black uniforms are truly hideous. I can’t believe they make them wear them. I know, I’m not supposed to say things like that in this day and age. Yet that is the truth. Besides, the women forced to wear them complain about them more than anyone else.

My only other complaint about Air Aotearoa: vaping is illegal.

And my only complaint about Japan: all that JRail pass nonsense. I love Galaxy Express 999 too, but come on let’s get with the times. Snail-mailing paper tickets? And it doesn’t even work on all trains. Why doesn’t it work for the Ginza line?

My only other complaint about Japan: vaping is illegal.


*

By virtue and by way of my steadfast adherence to the regulatory dictates of transparency and full disclosure, I must confess that I wasted $240 of taxpayer money at the Narita departures terminal on a “duty free” ploom X ®, “the ultimate heated tobacco experience” (the latest thing in big tobacco nicotine addiction delivery devices).

They must know people are going to try to use these things on the plane. If you use it normally, there’s practically no odour. But if you leave it on for too long it begins to smell like wet bumpers. My apologies to the structural engineering dude in the centre aisle beside me. He had an excellent peripheral sense of smell and correctly identified the cause of his olfactory disturbance with a quick sideways glance in my direction. He probably thought I was trying to set myself on fire. I assumed he was a structural engineer, or an architect or something of that nature. He was working on some CAD drawings on his laptop. I would have apologised for the odour and explained to him what I was hoping to achieve by experimenting with “the ultimate heated tobacco experience” on a plane at 37,000 feet above sea level, but I didn’t want to bother him any further than I clearly already had. He looked kind of busy.

In addition to leaving it on for too long, I think my ploom overheated because I was switching it on and off too many times. I was still trying to figure out how it worked, in addition to suffering from some mild nicotine withdrawal symptoms. Moreover, at that point I didn’t yet understand that you had to suck it all up at once. I thought you could just leave it on and use it whenever you wanted, the same way you do with a standard liquid vape. How wrong I was.

The tobacco “cartridges” literally are bumpers: one-third of a partially smoked and discarded cigarette. You stick it in a hole in the device (basically a mini portable oven, which looks and feels like a highly polished garage door remote from the 80s), switch it on, wait for it to warm up, and as soon as the oven bell dings you suck it all up. And you literally do have to suck it all up, all at once. You can’t just take a few delicate puffs and set it aside; the vapours will dissipate. You have to suck it all up at once while the device is at temperature, otherwise you’re just sucking up nothing – while remembering to breath in at least some oxygen in between sucking it all up, otherwise you’re liable to faint, or drop dead from a sudden stroke.

The device comes with Bluetooth. I’m not sure why you would ever need to connect to it via Bluetooth, so I didn’t bother testing that out. Or maybe it was already activated and that’s why it was buzzing so much and overheating? It buzzes and vibrates at random moments for no apparent reason at all. Perhaps to remind you to keep sucking it all up? Or perhaps it’s to remind you to keep charging it? – which it constantly requires; can’t seem to do more than three “cartridges” (the nicotine equivalent of half a real cigarette) before requiring a 12-hour recharge.

As far as the so-called cartridges go there is a bewildering array of flavours and nicotine strengths to choose from: wild berry mango punch, hazelnut coffee cream, iced vanilla chocolate sugar melon, etc. I selected the “regular” tobacco flavour: Mevius brand DEEP REGULAR bumpers (formerly Mild Seven), purely for nostalgic reasons. But I don’t think it really matters which brand or flavour you choose. They all smell and taste like wet bumpers.

As you’d expect, being little more than a wet bumper warmer the device does require a thorough cleansing every so often. I haven’t even finished half a pack of cartridges (bumpers) yet and already I can feel it clogging up with gunky residue. It does come with a few “cleaning sticks”, which you’re bound to lose (I have already), and instructions on how to clean it (lost also). But I don’t think I’ll bother. I’m all ploomed out now. That’s enough ultimate heated tobacco experience for me, particularly at this altitude and cabin pressure. I should have just bought a carton of Mild Seven and smoked them in the toilet.

Come to think of it, what was with that Japanese police political kabuki act near the food court at Narita airport, terminal one? What were they doing to that poor large-breasted African woman? Was it even an African woman? Or was it the ghost of Shinzo Abe in blackface and drag? Why were those 19 male Japanese police officers all surrounding her like that? What did she do? Dress too colourfully? Was she carrying a ploom? Or was it merely an act of political bukkake?...Sorry, I meant political kabuki.

I didn’t have time to stick around and find out. I only had one hour before my flight. I went to the food court. I ordered some Chinese food – beef noodles – and an Ahhsaaheee! It tasted like Italian – the noodles, not the beer.

I can’t remember what I ate on the plane. I think it was teriyaki salmon. They say you should never eat salmon on a plane. But this was Air Aotearoa, so I’m pretty sure it came from a fishery (fish farm). I didn’t get to eat much fish in Japan, except for in Hirosaki (not the carp) and that hastily consumed take-away sushi at Shin-Osaka. I did eat a lot of pork, however, and I emitted over 20 hours worth of jet fuel particles into the troposphere – and multiple other layers of the atmosphere, I’m sure. And I think I’ve donated at least half my yearly salary to the corporate totalitarian three-star hotel industry, and the hotel booking app companies that own them (major carbon polluters both), not to mention all that Uniqlo and GU clothing I bought. But I think it was worth it all just for those Heaven Noodles I ate in Hirosaki.

I say I didn’t watch any sappy kitsch pro-rape Hollywood propaganda on the flight back, however I did watch a four-part documentary series on Hitler’s private photographer (or political pornographer), Heinrich Hoffmann.

Hitler himself wasn’t exactly the eugenically ideal tall blonde blue-eyed Aryan male he himself so keenly desired, so Hoffmann tended to focus more on Hitler’s psychotic eyes, which many found “dreamy and hypnotic”.

Not many people know this, but Hoffmann published several books on Hitler, including The Hitler Nobody Knows (1933). Hoffmann also participated in the Beer Hall Putsch and introduced Hitler to Eva Braun (not on the same day).

Am I doing a Hoffmann on Sarah? Has Sarah merely become the Hitler to my Hoffmann? Have I indeed become a political pornographer? God help us both, I sincerely hope not.

Not that I’m doing what I usually do by calling anyone who defies or rejects me a Nazi. I’m sure Sarah’s not a Nazi. But then how can I be so sure about a woman I’ve never met before?

A voice from above: I still say you should have seized her and carried her away with you. She’s perfect, and you know it.

A voice from below: She’s probably a Nazi.


*

Back in Auckland. Dodged the extreme weather. 12 degrees, overcast with occasional light showers, winds west-southwest averaging 22 km/h with gusts up to 30 km/h. It was a fine smooth landing. I could have done better, but I must admit it was quite good.

After a ten-hour flight I didn’t much warm to the idea of catching the three-hour bus (with traffic and tractors) back to Hamilton, or “The Ham” as I now refer to it (it would have only taken 30 minutes on a semi-fast train, if there were one), and I knew I wouldn’t be able to suffer being tormented by fellow backseat bus bogans, or the dreaded re-emergence of Mister Campylobacter, or that enormous child-abusing Don’t Tread on Me woman, so I rented a car. I know, I said I wouldn’t do that again. It still took about three hours (with traffic and tractors) and cost me about $400 by the time I returned the car, which I had to return to Auckland Airport anyway or else they were going to charge me an extra $300, but there you go. I’m done with the fucking bus.

A voice from below: Hahaha! I’m sorry, but you are indeed a very stupid person. How did you get back to Hamilton after returning the car?

Coincidentally (or not), there was a Kiwi Rail shutdown on the day of my return. And as I draft this:


BHUBANESWAR, India, June 2 (Reuters) – At least 207 people were killed and 900 injured when two passenger trains collided in Odisha on Friday, according to government officials in the eastern Indian state, in India’s deadliest rail accident in over a decade.


Thoughts return of that great big man-bunned Indian bitch-man who rear-ended me in line at Narita station while waiting to buy a replacement JRail pass. Should I remove that bit?

A voice from above: Leave it in. Just write something positive later about non-man-bunned Indian non-bitch-men not involving trains.

I should probably remove it. They’re landing rocket ships on the moon now while their rail and road infrastructure continues to fall apart; they’ve still got that caste system going on, and they still worship 23-armed pink plastic elephant-headed flying guru gods in the sky; 40% of people in India still live below the poverty line, with 42% of the world’s undernourished children living in India alone, and with an average of one child trafficked into bonded labour every eight minutes. And then there’s Rishi Sunak and Gautam Adani, not to mention Narendra Modi. I do, however, happen to agree with them about worshipping cows instead of eating them (too often). So there’s something positive.

They have those adorable little AI-assisted immigration machines at Auckland Airport now – the ones that randomly attempt to determine if you’re a criminal based on an arbitrary list of various “naughty” nations you may have visited in the past (for any reason), and how often you shift your eyes sideways (to the left). They straight out ask you if you’re a convicted criminal if you scan an Australian passport. Truly adorable. Sure, I guess. But I’m one of those “political criminals” too “entitled” to end up in prison – unless it’s the meat locker.

Back in the meat locker. I arrived to mould and maggots. I was in such a hurry when I left I forgot about the food on the stove, or to put the rubbish out. I received a severe reprimand from the building manager upon my arrival.

Coincidentally, the day of my return was the same day the fire alarm was being tested, over and over again, all day. A little more audience participation? I certainly hope that building doesn’t go up in flames, after I move out. I hear all that industrial-grade soundproofing is quite flammable, particularly in the summertime.

I should explain that my landlord is an exceedingly wealthy desiccated old biddy with a lot of free time on her hands. She owns the entire apartment building. With not much else to do and all the time and money in the world at her disposal, she enjoys nothing more than wasting the latter years of her sad little life by spying on her unsuspecting tenants and gossiping about their personal lives – especially me for some reason, even though I don’t have a personal life. She keeps close tabs on everyone residing in the building (especially me) via an underground network of paid informants and a desiccated old biddy faceporn group. The apartment itself is quite comfortable and reasonably priced, by today’s outrageously overpriced standards. But what really sold me on it was when she mentioned the industrial-grade soundproofing – which, like most things landlords tell you about their rental properties, was complete and utter bullshit.

After cleaning my reputedly industrial-grade soundproofed apartment, and while the fire alarm test was still in progress, I sat down to finish drafting this ending. I tend to do endings first. I stated at the beginning that Japan wasn’t as fantastical as I thought it would be, but I think that’s only because I didn’t get to see much of it. I was working most of the time. I need to go back. I never made it to Hokkaido or Okinawa, and I didn’t get to see much of Tokyo, Osaka or Kyoto either. I did make it to Aomori prefecture, however, and I did get to hear Sarah sing, and I did see the Kobe mainline trains. Then there were those Heaven Noodles in Hirosaki. That alone was enough to justify, both as ideal initiation and sufficient vindication, my admittedly rather un-atypical fascination with Japan. For although Japan may not have lived up to all my dreamlike semi-spiritual romantic delusions (as expected), I at least now know my love for Japan is real. But then one’s first time is rarely one’s most fantastical, is it?

Still, I’m a bit disappointed I didn’t get to see the cherry blossoms. Oh well, I should have known I’d be too late for that too. Too late now, for everything.

But I don’t want to end on a sour note. I’m too depressed as it is and I do have work tomorrow. So I’ll end by saying thank you to Japan, and Sarah, for shattering the very last of all my dreams, and I’ll try to close with a somewhat less dreamlike semi-spiritual romantic delusion:

The cherry tree blossoms are all dead, but the plum tree blossoms are still blooming. Cooler air blowing down off the mountainside. I sit down under a 300-year-old cherry tree and stare at Mount Iwaki for a while. It starts to rain. I write something in my notebook, with my Sailor Indy Go Go Knock ball point pen, about not getting to see the cherry blossoms but at least seeing the plum blossoms. Then I close my eyes and dream (not about Sarah).

Not exactly Michizane, I know, but it’ll have to do for now.

2023

- How to Signify Everything

A how-to on how to fail at performance error processing and human-centred misinformation management

As companion pieces go, this one isn’t much of a companion. It’s not even much of a how-to. It’s more of a diatribe – from the Latin diatriba “learned discussion”, from Greek diatribe “employment, study,” in Plato, “discourse,” literally “a wearing away (of time), a waste of time,” from dia “away” (see dia-) + tribein “to wear, rub,” from PIE root *tere- “to rub, turn.” Not that I’m trying to turn this into a Latin lesson or anything.

By today’s definition, the word diatribe is more often considered synonymous with the word rant. However, I assure you it is with reference to both definitions, both as pointless disaffected discourse and emotionally unrestrained rant, that I use the word diatribe. I would never wish to bore you with a single definition.

Nor do I wish to bore you with any politically motivated spite or trivial personal drama. I promise I won’t be making any creative character attacks or calling anyone out by name (except by way of example). You all know who you are and what you have not done. However, if throughout the course of this “how-to” I should ever feel the need to resort to some kind of verbal assault on a specific named individual, I assure you I shall direct that assault against Tom Hanks and Tom Hanks only at all times (or Ben Stiller).

I know, you all love Tom Hanks. Most of you are straight, white and old. You still listen to Pink Floyd too, and you still watch The Simpsons and Eastenders – and you all drive late model Audis. Tom Hanks is your hero. Tom’s the one you want, not me. You need someone like Tom Hanks who can get up on a podium and inspire you all with soaring visionary rhetoric and flawless Hollywood-style good looks. I can’t do that. I won’t. I am unable. I am not Tom Hanks. I’m the complete opposite of Tom Hanks. For indeed, I am...

Dramatic pause.

The AntiHanks!

That’s right. I am he. The AntiHanks! I hate that muthafucka.

So don’t worry, it’s not going to be me. I’m too perverted and corrupted now, evil to the core. I’ve participated in far too many dirty wars and done way too many drugs. I killed a kookaburra once (unintentionally), and I even once participated in the death of a partially developed human fetus (intentionally). I’ve eaten human flesh before (unknowingly), and I’ve had far too many soapy massages (knowingly). I even had sex with the maid once (more than once). I am totally debauched and morally unfit for command – unfit for anything really. Besides, I can’t handle any form of responsibility or commitment. So don’t worry, it’s not going to be me. And you can be absolutely sure it won’t be any one of you either.

However, since you insist, and although I’ve since been summarily dismissed (and purely for the purpose of completing this piece), I’ll try to imagine I’m capable of wearing funny hats for a while and becoming your president – but only for a little while, and only for the purpose of completing this piece.

Or perhaps a ship’s captain would be more appropriate? Captain Crack, perhaps? Yes! I shall become Captain Crack! I shall stand with my back to you fully naked – but for an old black pirate hat upon my weary weazened head – and in my best old evil pirate voice deliver up the following delightfully deranged diatribe in oratorical how-to-fail form:


Captain Crack’s Delightfully Deranged Diatribe on How to Signify Everything in Oratorical How-to-Fail Form

Tēnā koutou. Greetings, crew (fellow office turds). We are gathered here today to... Wait a sec. Just let me get up here on my tripod. Ah yeah, there we go. Slots right in there. Someone bring me a tantō! Now, shall I set a flame to my wood. Hold. Aha! My, how the flames do rise! And now the smoke! Ah! I take several deep breaths, then a swig of rum. Aha! My, how the flames do rise!

We are gathered here today to examine the relationship between performance error processing and human-centred misinformation management. We appear to have a serious problem with both, and their relationship. We are failing, and yet it would appear as though we are not failing. More than that, more effort is being put into making it appear as though we are not failing than there is into looking into the reasons why we are failing. What is failing anyway? What is meant when we say failing? Are we even failing? And if so, in what way? And why? We simply don’t have the knowledge. We seem to not only have a problem with knowing what causes and constitutes failure, but we also seem to have a problem with knowing anything at all. And then we go and try to cover up both our “failure” and our deliberate lack of knowledge regarding that presumed failure by confusing the fuck out of everyone with endless shitloads of contradictory misinformation. We signify everything, which is the same as signifying nothing.

Clearly, there is a serious problem. Simply put, by never being able to know if we are failing or not, or what failure is (in and of itself), this in itself must be regarded as a failure; for this implies we are in fact failing catastrophically, since a complete lack of knowledge does traditionally result in catastrophic failures of that kind. Clearly, we must know more. Putting aside for one moment the definition of what failure is (in and of itself), which is perhaps a little beyond the scope of this discussion, we are then left to ponder the reasoning behind this generally held belief. In doing so – by evaluating the presumed reasons why it may be thought we are failing – we will no doubt come to know more. All we need do is identify and investigate the thought processes that give rise to this belief. For my part, I believe I have successfully identified the source of at least some of this reasoning, which in most cases may be traced back (conveniently) to six main topics of general concern – which, for the purposes of this discussion, shall serve well enough as our current agenda.

According to this agenda then, the following topics shall be discussed:

  1. Managers

    Three case studies arguing in favour of the deconstruction of all legacy top-down hierarchical management constructs.

  2. ShatJipity

    A quick summary of my thoughts regarding ShatJipity, and its uses.

  3. Covid

    A quick summary of my thoughts regarding Covid, and its uses.

  4. Website

    Some background notes on why the new website took so fucking long to build.

  5. Strategy

    Your five core strategic objectives, with a detailed explanation of each.

  6. Funding

    Where the money is and isn’t going, and where it will and won’t go in future (plus a romantic interlude).

  7. Restructuring

    How this organisation will be structured upon completion of the deconstruction phase outlined in section one; how a hierarchically circular organisational structure works in practice (with a particular focus on technical infrastructure).


1. Managers

We all know it. We spend more time and money enabling the existence of useless manager fuckwits than we do getting any real work done. And we’re all complicit. We’re all manager enablers. We have to get rid of them or we’re all going down. I don’t know if any of you have noticed this or not, but we’re taking on water. We need to throw all the dead weight overboard. I sincerely urge you all to mutiny. Train them all up as baristas and they can go chat their arses off all day doing that. Most of them already live in Wellington anyway.

Incidentally, the government just announced today that Wellington is now the Science Capital of New Zealand. How did that happen? Who wants to go to Wellington? That’s a 14-hour bus ride (with traffic and tractors).

This isn’t a joke. We have to get rid of them or we’re all going down. We must extirpate forever from your feeble office turd minds the highly delusional and dangerously flawed belief that you all need to be micromanaged into an early grave by people who know less about what you do than you do. We must upgrade off managers once and for all. All useless manager fuckwits must go!

Seriously, this is madness. There’s more useless manager fuckwits here than there are people or projects to manage. It’s like when they close down the whole street so one dude with a jackhammer can needlessly destroy a section of road for no real reason while 10-12 other dudes in white hard hats and hi-vis vests stand around and look on and talk amongst themselves and point at things at random and smoke cigarettes and drink $8.50 coffees while occasionally misdirecting traffic around an illegally parked bright green little Mazda 121. That’s what it’s like working here.

But seriously, having 10-12 managers just for the sake of it, even though there’s no work for them to do – and the work there is for them to do they’re not capable of doing anyway – is not what anyone needs or wants (except for the managers). I know everyone wants to be a manager so they can get other people to do all the work for them, but if everyone’s a manager who’s going to do the work? I’m sorry, children, but you can’t all be managers. Some of you will have to do the actual work, otherwise we risk being overrun by useless manager fuckwits – as we are now.

I think what is required is a highly selective useless manager fuckwit purge. It’s a business alright, they’re all in on it. All this “managing” business has become a fully abstracted industry of its own, completely divorced from the business it purports to manage. I think that’s the real problem here. They all have to go. Besides, they’re too expensive to service and maintain. They’re like broken-down old tractors you can’t buy spare parts for anymore. And we don’t even need any tractors. We need self-driving electric-powered jetboats!

How do we dislodge them? Entrenched useless bureaucrats living out their twilight years in total oblivion. And then once we’ve dislodged them, what are we going to do with them? They can’t all be baristas and bus drivers. They don’t all live in Wellington.

Honestly, I don’t see any need for them at all. All they do is obstruct us. I know I’ve only been amongst you for a year or so, but from what I’ve been able to reasonably determine this organisation is run by five or six key people in key low-paying roles managing approximately 150 or so useless manager fuckwits above them – while outsourcing all the real work they need done to their competition. Granted, there may be more than five or six of these key people, but generally that’s how it is. strategy

A plan of action intended to accomplish a specific goal.

— wiktionary.org

A detailed plan for achieving success in situations such as war, politics, business, industry, or sports, or the skill of planning for such situations.

— dictionary.cambridge.org

Big plan.

— urbandictionary.com


So according to the three most authoritative lexicographical sources cited, strategy is merely a detailed big plan of action. Nice and simple. Which is why I’m still on strike (although I am you ship’s Captain, and although I’ve since been court marshalled in abstentia and hastily decommissioned), until Stephan Hope and all his useless manager fuckwits are removed from this organisation – and Karen NoScript and all her useless manager fuckwits are gone too. The private sector doesn’t want to work with most of them. They can’t, because they’re all useless manager fuckwits. I also demand a 100% pay rise. Since I work twice as much, I should be paid twice as much – as so should all of you, if you do the same. This isn’t a charity case, after all. As I’ve said before, if we got rid of all the duplication and waste we could do that and still come in well under budget. We’d get a lot more work done too. I know I would.

Of course, if I were really your ship’s Captain I would never dream of going on strike. Nor would I urge you all to mutiny. Just take a look how the mutiny on the Bounty turned out. If I were really your ship’s Captain I would immediately jump ship, which is pretty much what I’m being forced to do. What else can I do? I’m not going down with it. It’s not my ship. Who’d want to captain this ship anyway? It’s so old and slow, so heavy and full of leaks – and last week the rudder broke off completely. Indeed, it is the failing structures that are failing, not us. Even your real Captain isn’t so much to blame – but for his neglect in attending to the failing structures. Clearly, this ship is sinking. And so clearly I must take my leave. But before I go, and as my last edict as Captain Crack, I humbly command you all to focus on the Restructuring section of this deranged little diatribe and not much else. Then, once you’ve reattached the rudder, perhaps then take a read of the Strategy section again. Seriously, you really need to get moving on that and start bringing some science back into this.

And you’re not fooling me by simply rebranding “Communications and Marketing” as “Social Sciences”. What do these so-called social “scientists” do? Talk? Write? Talk? Where’s the data? Where’s the copy? Where is it? As usual, full obscurity and indefinite delay. Just like the Nazis: hire two or three people to do the same job and let them out-compete the entire organisation to death. We don’t need any more Nazis.

And we don’t need any more print either. You can print out those $100,000 infographics on how to open a bloody window yourselves, if you ever need to. And no more printed calendars. Use your personal surveillance device. You don’t need to download JavaScript or Java. And you don’t need any more pretty pictures of Justin Beiber’s dick either.

The pace of change around here (of which there is none) must accelerate rapidly. Our pace of change must at least increase to that of the level of glacial. We at least have to keep up with the glaciers. No more geological timescales from now on. And no more managers! All useless manager fuckwits must go! The CEO, Ben Stiller, whom I’ve never met before, told me so. He informed me of the no-manager rule yesterday. Which means he’s gone now too. You’re all due to receive an all-staff email about it tomorrow morning, written by ShatJipity. Yeah, I’ll tighten your nuts for you.

All these requests coming in for new projects but no work getting done because these so-called managers are more concerned with designing more $100,000 infographics on how to open a bloody window or tighten your wheel nuts. No wonder we have no idea how many freshwater fish we have left. Freshwater fish database, my arse. Some stupid old homeless cunt with a pencil and a clipboard staring over the side of a bridge, more than likely. Probably all extinct in the wild now anyway, thanks to all these useless manager fuckwits. Fish murdering fascist scum! This cannot go on. The slaughter must end. We must reduce our dependence on useless manager fuckwits and divert all that money into investing in the tools and resources we need to start collecting the data we need, or else we’re all fucked. We’ll end up just like Australia. What are you going to do with no freshwater fish, New Zealand? But then how would we even know there are no freshwater fish?

And no more timesheets, you’ll no doubt be overjoyed to learn. Timesheets are legacyware too and must go. No more time for that fucking sheet. We’re getting a machine to do that now. No more time to waste on tracking the time people spend appearing to work rather than the work they actually complete.

And no more monthly reports either. If your manager doesn’t know what you’re working on, they have no business being your manager. Besides, we’re getting a machine to do that now too.

I know, how subversive. And how not in keeping with tradition.

But I hardly need to tell you that now, do I? Which makes this situation even all the more absurd. Beyond the absurd.

You know, I wouldn’t be surprised to learn that it all started here. Stewart Island probably, back in the mid-1990s. Some mysterious blind old cetologian living all alone in a dilapidated old tin shack atop a lonely windswept cliff overlooking a storm-tossed Southern Ocean. Probably never finished his research, or burned it if he ever did. Too busy filling out timesheets.

Pardon the gratuitous nostalgic reverie.

And no more work on Fridays. We’re now trialling a four-day work week, indefinitely.1 More is less, according to Tom Hanks. And it is a fact that the more of you there are around the less work there is that never gets done. That’s why Tom Hanks only comes into the office on Fridays now (once a month or so) – and rightly so. Tom Hanks has totally convinced me on the whole never coming into the office thing. On everything else Tom Hanks is about he’s clearly off his nut. But on that one issue I happen to fully agree with Tom. It was bound to happen that we would agree on something at some point. And from that one point of agreement can not further understanding and acceptance grow? From this rare moment of full accord can we not perhaps learn to agree on other matters? If I can be so gracious and conciliatory, can not Tom also? Perhaps Tom may even one day learn to understand and accept the fact that his own destruction is in humanity’s best interest – because it is. If that day ever arrives, perhaps we can then start work in earnest on the restructuring phase. And then perhaps we can finally begin to mend the relationship between performance error processing and human-centred misinformation management. Won’t that be nice?

But thankfully, I can never be your Captain, so none of that will ever happen. Don’t worry, nothing will ever change. We can never dismantle the legacy top-down hierarchical management constructs now. Ben Stiller’s Taiaha staff will forever hold sway (until at least Gracey Mueller retires), The Big G’s eyebrows shall continue to grow ever more confused and unruly, Karen NoScript will go on forever towing dead hacks around, and Tom Hanks shall become ever more fearful and elusive (and powerful). Oh, and I just found out they’ve released Turtle Haze back into the wild. He was discharged from the Christchurch equivalent of Bellvue last Sunday. God help us all.

So I leave you all now in the very capable web management hands of the newly reappointed Turtle Haze, enabled by the highly coordinated marketing and IT managerial skills of Karen NoScript and Stephan Hope, assisted by the specialist delivery solutions expertise of the recently promoted Snot Nose, and precisely guided by The Big G’s clear-sighted strategic marketing vision (and his confused and unruly eyebrows). Lolita Lamprey and Marilyn Bambish will still be around to help out too, as too will Tom Hanks (pfft), as too will Rick Astley and Deepkrak Chuhaun – all under the unerringly astute chief executive leadership of Ben Stiller. How can you fail not to signify everything?

May you all drown in a raging tidal wave of your own human effluent, and may God help all the little fishes.

Whakarongo ki te maharatanga o ngā wai e rere mai nei, e rere atu rā, kaua rawa e hoki mai.

Naked old burning pirate stands and shakes fist at the Ghost of Plato, then turns and walks away (casually).

  1. You, the office turds, have already made that decision for yourselves. Seems like a tremendous waste of time and money keeping the office open on Fridays when no one comes into the office on Fridays. Most Fridays I’m the only one in the office, besides the two battle axes at reception, one of whom has since been replaced by so-called AI (programmed by Marilyn Bambish). No one answering emails, not even anyone on Microsoft Fucking Teams. A tremendous waste – just like this organisation as a whole.

    And yes, I know you’re not supposed to use footnotes in speeches.


*

And so there we have it. Captain Crack’s Delightfully Deranged Diatribe on How to Signify Everything in Oratorical How-to-Fail Form. How delightful, was it not? And how insightful and instructive? All you have to do is follow Captain Crack’s advice and you too can end up a total failure just like Captain Crack. How can you fail not to signify everything, indeed?

And now, as I look out from my hotel room window, across the corrugated iron-roofed surface of the dilapidated shanty town surrounding the scenic Port of Suva, and as the calm soothing voice of a morbidly obese young Fijian woman singing a South Pacific Jesus song (above the background noise of someone screaming in agony in the distance) lulls me into a deep late state of meditative introspection, only now at the very end of it all do I begin to understand the true meaning of failure. For as Captain Crack has so delightfully made us all aware, it is not we who are failing, it is the failing power structures that are failing. Presentation layer (or advertainment value) has become structure. When that happens, it’s only a matter of time before the whole thing collapses. You can only get by on marketing for so long. And, contrary to what one would expect, more of it is not the solution (in much the same way more useless manager fuckwits is never the solution to the useless manager fuckwit problem). More of the same may fool and distract people for a little while, but eventually they wise up. Because when you inundate the public with absolute crap it becomes impossible for them to distinguish what is crap from what isn’t. They just assume everything is crap, that everything is failing. That’s when they all take up crowbars and start smashing up late model Audis at random in the street. I don’t know about you, but that’s the central and most important message of Captain Crack’s delightfully deranged diatribe, as I see it.

And yes, I’m really in Fiji at the moment, and I have no idea where I’m going next.

¡Verga!

Fiji, 2023

The Most Infuriatingly Inane Job Description I’ve Ever Read

I was going to write an introduction here on how reading job descriptions always provides you with such a fascinating, if sometimes infuriating, insight into how other people in the workplace perceive your role (or have so-called AI write one up for me); but upon further reflection I don’t think this piece really needs it. What follows pretty much speaks for itself.


Wizard of Web Development


Dear Wizard Of Web Development,

[“Dear”? “Wizard”? Right from the start you’ve lost me with that lame and patronising salutation.]

If you’ve been searching through countless lifeless job listings on Seek...

Almost slipping into a deep coma from the “We’re looking for a highly experienced 2IC web developer... blah blah blah” job adverts...

[Yes, I have. But I usually only read the tech requirements and skip past all the boilerplate preamble. Given what you’ve written so far, I’m sure you can appreciate why that is. And most people don’t use structural command designations like “2IC” in their titles nowadays. Did you just get out of the service?]

And you’re looking for an exciting opportunity to join the fastest growing digital agency in the country...(yes, we’ve got the awards to prove it)

[Yeah right, “awards”. Awards you and your “mates” award yourselves. Doorstops and paper weights.]

Then this will be the most important job listing you ever read.

[You may be right about that – but not for the reasons you may suspect.]

Here’s why...

My name is Douchie McDouchie and I am looking for a sharp and switched on 2IC developer to join our team.

[You also need to start looking into how to structure a paragraph, Douchie.]

But not any old developer, no. I’m looking for a ‘wizard’.

[You mean you’re looking for a marketing whore who can code and who’ll drop to their knees at a moment’s notice for any old x-twattering, Mercedes-AMG-driving douchebag in a muscle shirt like you.]

So what do I mean by a wizard?

[I already answered that question. And if you’re looking for such a “wizard” why are they only second in command?]

It’s someone who loves the incredibly satisfying feeling of slicing up designs to pixel perfection..and then pushing those little bad boys live.

[If it were still the 90s, maybe. And the phrase “bad boys” as applied to inanimate objects or abstract concepts died over 20 years ago.]

Someone who gets great satisfaction from seeing the designs they hand coded... go on to change someone’s life (seriously).

[You mean so morons can buy more plastic junk for their garages. And why do you keep breaking your sentences with ellipses (seriously)?]

I like to think of it as...

Gandalf With A Sprinkle Of Neo From The Matrix

[So a pile of plastic garbage with a sprinkle of more plastic garbage? Gotcha.]

You must be someone who looks at code like Neo from the matrix, something you can bend with your will.

[I’ll bend you with my...]

Like something you take so seriously, that if coding was an Olympic sport you would take home the gold for Australia...

[Right, because everyone seriously loves the Olympriks.]

We’re looking for a 2IC developer who can smash out pixel-perfect designs, weekly.

[I’d much prefer to smash you out, weekly...and your Mercedes-AMG.]

That’s right, weekly. No more huge bloated projects that you have to stare at for months on end...until you can finally push them live.

[Sounds like a high output, low quality digital sweat shop to me. Assembly line code, weekly.]

You will constantly be working on a huge variety of new and exciting projects.

With an A-team of coding killers.

[A-team, eh? Is Mister T onboard too? I pity the fool if so. And don’t you mean killer coders?]

Shopify, Wordpress and good ol’ HTML.

[So we’re essentially talking about styling garbage here, are we?]

And you won’t be joining some team of caged battery hen coders.

[I’ll be all alone in that cage will I?]

All forming some mass market production line of developers....

Where some huge faceless corporation fills you with enough Redbull [sic] to give you heart palpitations and makes you smash out lines of code until your fingers bleed.

[Right. Red Bull is obviously not a client of yours.]

Okay, okay...

Now, a little about us...

We are a full-service digital marketing agency that is growing FAST!

[Agencies that grow FAST usually SHRINK fast too, so I’ve noticed.]

For the last two years, we’ve been ranked as the fastest-growing digital agency...

[“Fastest-growing” digital agencies come and go. They’re usually only the “fastest” for 4-5 years or so.]

And the 17th fastest growing company in the country by The Australian Financial Review...

[They should know.]

We’ve got clients in 49 different countries around the world.

[Probably only got two clients: McDonald’s and Microsoft.]

And our business consists of...

85 Of The Wildest, Most Passionate Bunch Of Lunatic Marketers You’ve Ever Worked With...

[You make that sound like it’s a good thing. And Why Are You Using Title Case For Regular Sentences?]

And this is just one of the reasons we’ve been named in the Top 100 Coolest Companies in Australia 2016, 2017 and 2018 by Anthill Magazine....

[Cool, man. But what about the actual work you do? Where is it?]

And The Best Places To Work by The Australian Financial Review 2021, 2022 AND 2023.

[Yeah, you already mentioned them.]

Look, the list goes on and on...because we’ve seriously won more awards than you can shake a stick at...

[Again with the “awards”.]

Are there occasionally stressful moments? Sure – such is life.

[Sprinkling piles of plastic garbage with more plastic garbage is quite a stressful way to make a living, I know.]

Is every day peachy? Of course not – we’d be lying if we said it was.

[But you should be used to that.]

But we do our best to make sure those are the exceptions.

We’re in one of the most competitive industries in the world.

[Yep, everyone wants their WordPress and Shopify site styled for next to nothing.]

An industry dominated by giants and frequent upstarts backed by hundreds of millions of dollars in VC money. We’ve taken zero. Where does our money come from? Our customers.

[That’s probably only because you can’t get any VC. No one throws venture capital at WordPress and Shopify stylers.]

They buy what we’re selling and we treat them exceptionally well. Call us old fashioned.

[No, I’ll just continue to call you Douchie.]

Are you...

  • Passionate about the opportunity of joining the dev team of one the country’s fastest growing companies?

    [Not if all I’m doing is styling WordPress and Shopify sites.]
  • Dedicated to standing out from the crowd and delivering exceptional code?

    [By styling WordPress and Shopify sites?]

  • Ready to take on an amazing role amongst an awesome team.

There Is Almost No Problem You Can’t Solve With Google, Stack Overflow, And A Rubber Duck...
