Open Letter to Taylor Swift (Or How Not to Drive Three Maseratis at Once Down a Dead End Street)

On the socio-political reverberations of Taylor Swift’s cultural prominence: intersecting the corrupted intersections between art, entrepreneurship and industry

Taylor,

I never thought I’d ever become a “Swiftie”, yet here we are. But to be honest, I haven’t listened to much of your music. It’s not really my kind of thing. I’m more of an Emma Kirkby kind of dude. However, I do quite like some of what I have listened to so far, particularly that “Anti-Hero” song of yours. Overall, I quite like your music, and your politics, and you seem like a perfectly lovely person in every other respect – and I stand with you against all those stupid people who constantly attack your boobs. But rest assured this has nothing to do with your boobs. This is about the corrupted intersections.

I don’t know too much about you personally either. I know you’re into pop culture, tight ends and ball handlers and you’re still in you’re mid-20s, or something ridiculous like that. However, I do know that you’re a billionaire and that you own three Maseratis. I’d much prefer you weren’t a billionaire. But I suppose I can overlook that. I’d much prefer you weren’t white either, or an American. But I’ll try to overlook all that too. I also know you were named after James Taylor. Excuse me for saying so, but I think you’re more like the reincarnation of Hank Williams – without the alcoholism and drug abuse, one would hope. Although, you did make it past the age of 29, so perhaps no need to hope.

Yet despite your godlike stature, Taylor, I must confess I’m not in love with you. I’m still in love with Sarah (more than ever), truth be told – even though I’ve recently discovered she’s a Nazi. Of course, I’m only saying she’s a Nazi because I know she doesn’t love me – and because she likes to sing Billy Joel songs – I know that. But then, like you, she is a commercialised celebrity, and you’re allowed to say anything you want about commercialised celebrities these days, even if it isn’t true.

You’re probably used to that too, so I’m sure you understand my motivation. And I’m also sure you understand that it really doesn’t matter what I say about Sarah, or you. It’s not like my opinion matters. Besides, as with everything I’ve written to Sarah, you’ll more than likely never get a chance to read or reply to this letter.

Therefore, since you’ll never have a chance to read or reply to this letter, I thought I’d structure it as a series of frustratingly unanswerable dumb questions you’ll never have the opportunity to answer. How annoying, right? It’s like driving my pickup truck by your house and sticking my head out the window and constantly hollering your name but never stopping or even slowing down to allow you to jump in. Not that you would ever wish to anyway.

How do you feel about populist commercialism and the cult of celebrity, Taylor? Do you believe it’s in any way tolerable that commercial success and talent rarely equate in the advertainment industry? Do you think it’s at all acceptable that fossilised throwback rocktards and hypersexualized plastic poptarts earn outrageous sums of money for pumping out all that repetitive puerile garbage while most real musicians can’t even make a living? Have you ever just stood and stared into space for long periods of time and marvelled at the thought of all that music never to be made or heard due to that fact? I know I have.

Of course, I’m no way referring to you in any of those dumb questions above. I know you know who and what I’m referring to. You fought them and won – more than won – when most of us lose. Those of us who lose have no choice but to live the dream through you. You’re a living dream, Taylor, in a dying world where most of our dreams are already dead. For that reason, and if only for that reason, I can understand your appeal. You are the dream we should all be living. Admittedly, that only one of us is living that dream (you) seems a bit unfair to me, all things considered. But then life’s always been that way, hasn’t it?

The Rapist in Chief claims it was the Music Modernization Act – signed into law on October 11, 2018 – that enabled you to become the first ever billionaire from the sale of music alone. As with most successful women, there’s usually a man willing to come along and take all the credit. How does that make you feel?

And how do you feel about being constantly stalked and personally attacked just for writing and singing songs? How do you deal with that? I don’t think I could ever deal with it. I can’t even deal with what I’m writing now. In fact, as soon as I’m done writing this letter I’m changing my name to ℘ and I’m never writing, playing or even listening to music ever again...like, ever.

You’re frontpage news every day now, Taylor – even if it is only something about some Italian restaurant you dined at recently, that you like to visit zoos and watch the kangaroos, or the fact that you’re distantly related to Emily Dickinson. Don’t you find that extremely annoying? I know I do. By the way, I’ve been in love with Emily Dickinson since I was 23. She was a reclusive lesbian who was in love with her sister, so they say. I could have turned her. But since Emily’s been dead for the last 140 years or so I’ve decided to focus on you. I have no one else to write to now anyway.


The Bat is dun, with wrinkled Wings –
Like fallow Article –
And not a song pervade his Lips –
Or none perceptible.


I’m really done once I finish writing this letter. Henceforth, not one more song, perceptible or otherwise, shall pervade my lips. I still have a few fallow articles to clean up as well. But once I’ve completed that and this letter is written, that’s it. I’m done.

And although I know I’m too late to submit this letter to Melbourne University’s 2024 Swiftposium: an academic conference on Taylor Swift (seriously, it’s a real thing), I’m still going to finish writing it regardless. I doubt I would have won a prize anyway. I’ve used the word boobs too many times, for one thing. But this isn’t about wining or prizes, or boobs; that’s not what this is about. It’s about you, Taylor; it’s about you becoming who you were born to be and saving us all from certain doom.

In short, you must become a politician and replace Joe. Yes, you must run for President against the Rapist in Chief. It’s time to face facts. The face of nature is flawed with omens. We can all see it. Can you not see it also? He did a good enough job at restabilising the nation after the Rapist in Chief’s insurrection, but now it’s time for Joe to go. I will not suffer a second act of the Rapist in Chief. It would mean the immediate cancellation of our support contact. You must run for President, Taylor. Don’t worry, I’ll support you. With the right algorithm anything is possible these days.

You’ve already conquered the advertainment industry, now it’s time for you to conquer politics (which is pretty much the same thing). You admitted as much yourself in that “Anti-Hero” song of yours:


Did you hear my covert narcissism I disguise as altruism,
like some kind of congressman?


Yes, I did.

Did you hear my overt socialism I disguise as nihilism, like some kind of song and dance man?

Hank Williams was a song and dance man. Still, he had no problem jumping straight into politics. That “No, No, Joe” song of his is a prime example. And since you are the reincarnation of Hank Williams, it’s only natural that you do the same. Do you not agree?

But first you’ll have stop drinking alcohol and taking drugs (not that you do), never dance or have sex again, adopt a wholefoods plant-based diet, stop flying in private jets, sell your three Maseratis and donate the proceeds to charity, and stop dressing like a mermaid.

I love mermaids, by the way.

But seriously, how does it feel to know you have the largest carbon footprint of any person who has ever existed? Not just going by all the time you spend in private jets flying all over the world, but also with respect to your private army of “Swifties”, who travel from far and wide to attend your shows and stay in corporate chain hotels watching Nutflex “movies” while consuming vast quantities of ultra-processed fast fat foods.

Notwithstanding all that, and however much I do appreciate the socio-political reverberations of your cultural prominence, Taylor, I have no intention of attending your show here in Narrm (Melbourne). I don’t want to drop dead from heat exhaustion or get struck by lightning. Besides, I really don’t like crowds and I’d probably end up getting scammed or hacked if I ever tried to buy a ticket. But I do plan on listening to all of your songs at some stage. I’m holding off on that for now, since most of your songs make me feel incredibly sad. Most of your songs are about romantic relationships, of some form or another. I’ve never had much luck with that kind of thing.

Don’t worry, I assure you I am in no way romantically inclined towards you. I’m old enough to be your father – if I had of impregnated some poor unfortunate woman while still in my teens. And I do apologise if I sound rather forward and insistent, but unlike most of our contemporaries, 140 years from now you will still be remembered. Given that knowledge, I have no choice now but to slow down and stop at the corrupted intersections. Granted, I don’t have much of a pickup truck. It’s old, small and rusty and doesn’t have much power. But it is in surprisingly good mechanical condition, considering its age and general level of previous misuse.

It must be difficult driving three Maseratis at once. Don’t you want to go for a ride, Taylor?

You are quite tall, aren’t you? I believe a bar must be set to keep all the shorties out of politics. You must be this tall to ride this ride, etc. You are quite tall. Do you recall what Kundera wrote about tall women? But then Kundera was a womaniser, if not a straight-up misogynist, so I guess it doesn’t matter.

More importantly, have you ever read Anna Karenina? I haven’t. I’ve been meaning to for quite some time but just haven’t got around to it yet. Perhaps that’s for the best. Most things Russian tend to leave a bad taste in my mouth these days, and most of Tolstoy’s writing too is about romantic relationships of some form or another. Besides, there’s far too much going on in the real world these days. Sadly, I just don’t have the time to read Tolstoy.

The Underwear Poisoner finally had Alexei Navalny (the true President of Russia) murdered while you were playing your Narrm (Melbourne) show, the largest of your career. It’ll only get worse once The Rapist in Chief is back in office. Assange is probably next, then the rest of us.

(You have until the 5th of November, 2024.)

You must stand with me against The Underwear Poisoner and his Rapist in Chief, Taylor, before it’s too late. You must become a politician and run for president. It’s the only way to uncorrupt the corrupted intersections. Or else we’re cancelling “stan culture”, forever. Seriously, we can do that now.

You’re the perfect person for the job, Taylor, and the perfect age. We need to skip a generation. Those of my generation are peculiarly unsuited for politics. I believe it’s primarily because we came of age during the rise of the internets. Now we’re way too immersed in misinformation to distinguish what is real from what isn’t – under-reporting livestock numbers and firearm fatalities like it’s nobody’s business, and still using Domino Notes and FrontPage 98 like it’s still 1998. Yet precisely for that reason (the internets) are we peculiarly suited to provide a key supporting role when it comes to U.S. presidential elections. Better us than The Underwear Poisoner, do you not agree? Not to overlabour an obvious point of conspiratorial hermeneutics, but I believe this is precisely what is required. And I’m almost 87% certain most of my contemporaries would agree with me. Sorry, Taylor, but the power of assumed majority consensus compels you. You must be president.

All we need is the right algorithm.

Traditionally, most Americans got most of their politics from Fox “News” or MSNBC (Southpark and The Simpsons) and late night talk shows. Now they get all their politics from TitKok, X-twatter and faceporn (and “movies”, of course). Still, only around half of all eligible voters turn out to vote in most U.S. presidential elections. They’re far more interested in football and your boobs, and romantic relationships (and “movies”, of course). Politics is just like the advertainment industry in that respect: it’s not about the truth, it’s about marketing inane distractions and artificially concocted alternate realities.

Not so in my case, sadly. Despite the unrewarding futility of it, I prefer to work for a living, and I don’t have any romantic relationships – no personal relationships of any kind at all, in fact. And I suppose that’s why I’m writing to you about all these socio-political matters right now instead of living a real life, or reading Tolstoy.

So since I have no personal life and I’m not reading Tolstoy right now – and since I don’t have any romantic relationships to write about – I wrote you a silly little socio-political song about Tolstoy instead.


Tolstoy cares only for the growing
nice juicy sausages and big red roses
and you only ever create if you can care
for only bad children rebel against authority
and good-tempered antinomianism is nothing
but a dilapidated Parthenon of overlaboured designs
therefore I swear to never read or mention Tolstoy ever again.


In any event, these days I’m far too busy progressing the sustained and consistent delivery of enterprise outcomes while attending further planning meetings to discuss how to replay a retrospective of recent delivery learnings that can uplift big data portfolio integration planning via the adoption of new business tools within the broader enterprise as part of the Open Source business architecture migration phrase, which may potentially become possible enabling roadmaps in further big data planning meetings – while still using Domino Notes and FrontPage 98. So I really don’t have time to read any more Tolstoy, nor for romantic relationships.

Don’t worry if you don’t really understand that paragraph above. I don’t understand it either, even though I wrote it. I’ve been reading and writing paragraphs like that all my working life and I still don’t understand what they mean. That’s what happens when you spend an entire lifetime working in the misinformation technology industry and have no time to read Tolstoy, nor for romantic relationships.

Do you not see now why you must run for president, Taylor? Who will defend us against The Underwear Poisoner and his Rapist in Chief? Who will help us uncorrupt the corrupted intersections? Who else but you and your three Maseratis?

Love always, some idiot you’ve never heard of...and never will.

Elegy for Richard Simmons (1948-2024)

I don’t care how many fake Rapist in Chief assassination events they stage (even if Tom Hanks is the guest speaker). In my memory, July 13 shall forever be remembered as the day Richard Simmons passed away (unexpectedly).


Richard Simmons, age 76, of Los Angeles, California passed away unexpectedly [?], on Saturday, July 13, 2024. Born Milton Teagle Simmons on July 12, 1948 in New Orleans, Richard “Dicky” is predeceased by his parents, Leonard Douglas Simmons and Shirley Satin Simmons. He is survived by his loving brother and sister-in-law, Lenny and Cathy Simmons of Harahan, Louisiana and the hundreds of thousands of adoring fans whose lives he touched for over fifty years. Richard attended St. Louis Cathedral Parochial Grammar School, then graduated from Cor Jesu (now known as Brother Martin) High School, in 1966. He attended University of Southwestern Louisiana (now known as University of Louisiana at Lafayette) and graduated from Florida State University in 1970 with a Bachelor of Fine Arts degree. Known for his vibrant spirit and enduring passion for fitness, Richard never considered himself a celebrity, but rather a motivator who honestly cared about the people he met during his lifetime. His encouragement, positive attitude and trademark tank top and striped shorts made people all over the world, smile and laugh. He encouraged people of all shapes and sizes to “Never give up” and “move those buns”, because “You are worth it!” Please join us for a celebration of his incredible life on Saturday, October 5, 2024 with a Mass at St. Louis Cathedral for 11:00 am (doors open at 10:00 am). After Mass, there will be a brief workout tribute to “Sweating to the Oldies I” followed by a Second Line procession though his beloved French Quarter to Musicians’ Legend Park.

Published by The Times-Picayune from Sep. 27 to Sep. 29, 2024.


Last night I watched Richard Simmon’s funeral mass, broadcast live from St. Louis Cathedral. Richard’s brother Lenny did a pretty good job at the eulogy. Lenny told us all how Richard believed that God has a plan for all of us, and how Richard got his first acting break on General Hospital. Lenny also went on to explain how Richard’s fitness programs have positively changed the lives of millions of people all over the world – which, at the end of the day, must stand as Richard’s most enduring legacy. I thought I’d just take a moment to further expand on that legacy by adding a few statistical details of my own, and perhaps also make comment upon some of these other less important contemporaneous events of a “political” nature.

Some say the Republican party timed their fake assassination event to coincide with the death of Richard Simmons. Some say the Republican party straight-out assassinated Richard Simmons. Who knows what to believe. “Political” people are always so full of shit. But whatever the truth, in my mind no amount of far-right deep state stagecraft can ever detract from the significance of Richard Simmon’s lasting legacy. Richard’s positive impact on the health and well-being of millions of people all over the world is truly immeasurable. He helped humanity lose approximately 12 million pounds (5.5 million kg). When we convert that into CO2 emissions saved over the span of an average human lifetime that comes out to about... Well, to be honest, I don’t know how you would even begin to calculate that. But I’m sure it’s a lot. Indeed, Richard Simmon’s impact is truly immeasurable.

I say we make July 13 Richard Simmons Memorial Day. He was born July 12, so we could make that a holiday too and have a four-day Richard Simmons Memorial weekend. We could all wear tank tops and stripped shorts and workout to “Sweating to the Oldies” for four days straight. Think of all the CO2 emissions we’d save.

And however quaint and unnecessary it is to say, I must also say I reject all forms of so-called political violence. Violence is violence, political or not. Besides, there’s a place for all these “political” people. It’s called prison.

Move those buns! They’re worth it!
